147th Meeting of the Legislative Yuan

Passes the Zhejiang Province Debt Clearance Bond Regulations

The Legislative Yuan held its 147th meeting at 8:00 AM on the 21st. Thirty members including Shi Shangkuan attended. Shao Yuanchong, acting President of the Yuan, presided. The matters for discussion were as follows: (1) Deliberation on the draft Stamp Tax Law, resolved to be referred to the Finance Committee for review. (2) Report by the Legal Committee of the Yuan on the draft revision of the Organizational Regulations of the Relief Commission, resolved to be revised and passed. (3) Deliberation and approval of the Agreement on Treatment of Chinese Nationals Going to Nicaragua and its annexes, resolved to be referred to the Foreign Affairs Committee for review. (4) Deliberation on the draft Postal Savings Law, resolved to be revised and passed. (5) Deliberation on the draft Postal Domestic Remittance Law, resolved to be revised and passed. (6) Draft Organizational Law of the Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau, resolved to be revised and passed. The Postal Insurance Law should be drafted by the Ministry of Communications and submitted to the Yuan for review. (7) Report by the Finance Committee of the Yuan on the review of the revision of Articles 7 and 9 of the Organizational Law of the National Government's Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics, resolved to be passed as is. (8) Report by the Finance Committee of the Yuan, together with the Economic Committee, on the review of the Draft Regulations and Repayment Schedule for the Public Debt for Clearing Old Debts in Zhejiang Province in the 20th Year of the Republic of China, resolved to be revised and passed. (9) Revision of Article 9 of the Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Debt Regulations of the 20th Year of the Republic of China, resolved to be revised and passed. The appendix to Article 9 of the Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Debt Regulations is as follows: "The principal and interest of this public debt shall be paid by the Ministry of Finance ordering the Jianghai Customs to levy an additional national currency of 30 yuan per picul on the export of raw and white silk from Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces from the date of issuance of the public debt as a fund for repayment of principal and interest, which shall be deposited monthly into a special account by the Public Debt Fund Management Committee and paid on schedule until the principal and interest are fully repaid."

Passed by the Legislative Yuan

Various Articles on Postal Matters

At yesterday's (20th) 147th meeting of the Legislative Yuan, various articles of the Postal Savings Law were revised and passed. The details are recorded separately as follows:

Postal Savings Law (Article 1) Postal savings affairs shall be handled by the Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau established by the Ministry of Communications. (Article 2) The deposit and withdrawal of postal savings shall be limited to the national currency or the local common silver coins. (Article 3) For postal savings, one person or one group may only have one savings account. If the postal savings institution discovers that a person or a group has more than two savings accounts, all except the initial one shall be terminated and the principal shall be returned without interest. (Article 4) Postal savings can be divided into four types: passbook savings, checking savings, fixed savings, and transfer savings. (Article 5) For passbook savings, each deposit must be at least one yuan. If it is less than one yuan, the depositor should first obtain a savings grid paper from the postal savings institution and successively purchase and paste stamps. When the grid is full, the deposit is made. (Article 6) The total amount of each passbook savings account is limited to 3,000 yuan. Interest will not be paid on the amount exceeding the limit. The above restriction does not apply to government agencies, autonomous organizations, or public welfare legal entities. (Article 7) When postal savings are deposited for the first time, the depositing bureau shall issue a booklet or receipt according to its type. Subsequent deposits and withdrawals shall be based on the passbook or receipt. (Article 8) Passbooks and receipts for postal savings depositors shall not be added, annotated, or altered without authorization. (Article 9) Depositors' savings may be subsequently deposited or withdrawn from any postal savings institution within the unified savings area. The unified savings area and its measures shall be drafted by the Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau and approved by the Ministry of Communications. (Article 10) Passbook savings and checking savings may be withdrawn at any time, but if an individual withdraws 500 yuan or more from a passbook savings account at one time, the postal savings institution may require the withdrawer to notify them one day in advance. (Article 11) If a depositor has not made any deposits, withdrawals, or other requests within five years, the postal savings institution shall promptly notify the depositor to withdraw the savings and stop paying interest from the date of expiration of the five-year period. (Article 12) The measures for transfer savings are as follows: 1. Anyone may request the postal savings institution to transfer cash into the account of a transfer savings depositor. 2. Transfer savings depositors may request the postal savings institution to transfer savings to each other. 3. Transfer savings depositors may request the postal savings institution to pay cash to others with their savings. (Article 13) The principal and interest of postal savings are guaranteed by postal assets. (Article 14) The Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau shall publicly announce the entire balance sheet every five months. (Article 15) The interest rate, settlement method, and scope of use of postal savings shall be drafted by the Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau and submitted to the Supervisory Committee for determination. (Article 16) Interest on passbook savings shall be exempt from all taxes. (Article 17) The acts of persons without capacity for conduct and persons with limited capacity for conduct related to postal savings matters in postal savings institutions shall be regarded as acts of persons with capacity for conduct. (Article 18) The implementing rules and various savings regulations of this law shall be formulated by the Ministry of Communications. (Article 19) This law shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Postal Domestic Remittance Law (Article 1) Postal remittance affairs shall be handled by the Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau established by the Ministry of Communications. (Article 2) The remittance and fees of postal remittance shall be limited to the national currency or the local common silver coins. (Article 3) Postal remittances shall be divided into three types: ordinary remittance, telegraphic remittance, and small amount remittance. (Article 4) The limits on the amount of postal remittances shall be determined by the Ministry of Communications. (Article 5) Postal remittances shall be based on postal money orders. (Article 6) Money orders shall not be added, annotated, or altered without authorization. (Article 7) The post office may order the presenter to provide necessary proof in order to investigate the authenticity of the receiver. (Article 8) The effective period of money orders shall be determined by the Ministry of Communications according to the type and distance of the location, but shall not be less than three months. (Article 9) If the money order is not collected within the effective period, the post office shall return it to the original office and notify the remitter to collect it. In the aforementioned situation, the remitter shall not request a refund of the remittance fee. (Article 10) If a money order is lost or damaged, the remitter or receiver may request the post office to issue a duplicate money order. Once a duplicate money order is issued, the original money order shall be invalid. (Article 11) In the event of the situation in Article 9, Paragraph 1, if the remitter does not collect the remittance, the money order shall be canceled after three years from the date of issuance of the money order, and the remittance shall be collected as public money. (Article 12) Postal remittances shall be exempt from all taxes. (Article 13) The acts of persons without capacity for conduct and persons with limited capacity for conduct related to postal remittance matters in postal remittance institutions shall be regarded as acts of persons with capacity for conduct. (Article 14) The implementing rules and various remittance regulations of this law shall be formulated by the Ministry of Communications. (Article 15) This law shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Postal General Bureau Organizational Law (Article 1) The Postal General Bureau, directly under the Ministry of Communications, manages national postal affairs and directs and supervises the postal administrations of various provinces and regions. (Article 2) The Postal General Bureau shall have one Director-General, appointed with simplified procedures, who shall, upon the order of the Minister of Communications, manage the affairs of the Bureau comprehensively. There shall be one Deputy Director-General, who shall be appointed and employed by the Minister of Communications to assist the Director-General in handling the affairs of the Bureau. (Article 3) The Postal General Bureau shall have five departments: General Affairs, Accounting, Planning, International Postal Affairs, and Supply. Each of the aforementioned departments shall have one Director and one Deputy Director, who shall be selected from among the Postal Directors and Deputy Postal Directors by the Director-General and submitted to the Minister of Communications for appointment, and shall, upon the order of their superiors, manage the affairs of their respective departments. (Article 4) The Postal General Bureau may have one Chief Secretary and two to four Secretaries, who shall be selected by the Director-General and submitted to the Minister of Communications for appointment, and shall, upon the order of their superiors, handle clerical matters. (Article 5) The Postal General Bureau shall have 100 to 130 staff members, who shall be selected and employed by the Director-General from among postal staff members and postal assistants of all levels, and shall, upon the order of the Director, handle the affairs of the various departments. (Article 6) The Postal General Bureau shall prepare a budget of annual income and expenditure each year and submit it to the Ministry of Communications for review and transfer. (Article 7) At the end of the accounting year, the Postal General Bureau shall prepare a statement of final accounts of annual income and expenditure and submit it to the Ministry of Communications for review and transfer. (Article 8) All income and expenditure of the Postal General Bureau shall be in the name of the Postal General Bureau and shall be co-signed by the Director-General and the Deputy Director-General. (Article 9) The Postal General Bureau shall submit the regulations and contracts regarding postal affairs to the Ministry of Communications for approval. ((Article 10) The rules of procedure for the Postal General Bureau shall be determined by the Ministry of Communications. (Article 11) This law shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau Organizational Law (Article 1) The Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau, directly under the Ministry of Communications, manages national postal savings and remittance affairs. (Article 2) The Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau shall designate post offices in various places to handle local business. However, branch offices may be established in important transportation locations with the approval of the Executive Yuan upon submission by the Ministry of Communications. The Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau has the power to direct and supervise the handling of postal savings and remittance affairs by various post offices. (Article 3) The Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau shall have one Director-General, appointed with simplified procedures, who shall, upon the order of the Minister of Communications, manage the affairs of the Bureau comprehensively. There shall be two Deputy Director-Generals, who shall be appointed and employed by the Minister of Communications to assist the Director-General in managing business and accounting affairs. (Article 4) The Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau shall have seven departments: General Affairs, Business, Accounting, Savings, Remittance, Transfer, and Insurance. Each of the aforementioned departments shall have one Director and one Deputy Director, who shall be appointed and employed from the senior officials of the Ministry of Communications, and shall, upon the order of their superiors, manage the affairs of their respective departments. (Article 5) The Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau shall have one Chief Secretary and two to four Secretaries, who shall be selected by the Director-General and submitted to the Minister of Communications for appointment, and shall, upon the order of their superiors, handle clerical matters. (Article 6) The Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau shall have 60 to 80 staff members, who shall be appointed and employed by the Director-General to handle the affairs of the various departments upon the order of the Director. (Article 7) The Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau shall prepare a budget of annual income and expenditure each year and submit it to the Ministry of Communications for review and transfer. (Article 8) At the end of the accounting year, the Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau shall prepare a statement of final accounts of annual income and expenditure and submit it to the Ministry of Communications for review and transfer, and shall also publish various reports. (Article 9) From the annual postal savings and remittance net surplus, 30% shall be used as a public reserve fund and special reserve fund, and the remainder shall be reported to the Ministry of Communications and included in the postal revenue. (Article 10) All income and expenditure of the Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau shall be in the name of the Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau and shall be co-signed by the Director-General and the Deputy Director-General. (Article 11) The Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau shall have a Supervisory Committee, whose members shall be specially appointed by the National Government and shall consist of three persons, as well as the Minister of Communications, the Minister of Finance, the Minister of Audit, and the Director of the Postal Department of the Ministry of Communications. The rules for the aforementioned Supervisory Committee shall be determined by the Executive Yuan. (Article 12) The rules of procedure for the Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau shall be determined by the Ministry of Communications. (Article 13) This law shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Regulations for Clearing Old Public Debts in Zhejiang Province

Approved by the Legislative Yuan Meeting

Yesterday, the 147th meeting of the Legislative Yuan revised and approved the Regulations for Clearing Old Public Debts in Zhejiang Province in the 20th year of the Republic of China. The articles are as follows: Article 1: The Zhejiang Provincial Government, in order to clear various old debts, will issue public bonds of 8 million yuan, named the "Zhejiang Provincial Public Debt for Clearing Old Debts in the 20th Year of the Republic of China." Article 2: The interest rate of this public debt is set at 8% per annum. Article 3: This public debt will be issued at 98% of its face value. Article 4: This public debt is scheduled to be issued on July 1st of the 20th year of the Republic of China. Article 5: This public debt will pay interest twice a year, on June 30th and December 31st. Article 6: Starting from December of the 20th year of the Republic of China, this public debt will be repaid over ten years using a lottery method, with two drawings per year, until June 30th of the 30th year of the Republic of China, when all principal and interest will be fully repaid. The aforementioned lottery will be held annually on June 15th and December 15th, and payments will begin at the end of that month. The Ministry of Finance and the Audit Department will send personnel to supervise each lottery. Article 7: The number of bonds to be drawn and the amount of principal to be repaid each time are as specified in the attached schedule (schedule omitted). Article 8: 1.2 million yuan will be allocated annually from the Zhejiang Province deed tax and business tax revenue to serve as a fund for principal and interest repayment of this public debt. Article 9: The principal and interest fund for this public debt should be specially deposited in banks such as the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and local Zhejiang banks, and managed by the Fund Management Committee. The aforementioned Fund Management Committee will be organized by one representative each from the Provincial Government and the audit agency, as well as one representative each from the Bankers Association, the Money Industry Association, and the Chamber of Commerce. The management rules will be formulated separately. Article 10: The bonds for this public debt will be in three denominations: 1,000 yuan, 100 yuan, and 10 yuan, all in bearer form. Article 11: The Central Bank, the Bank of China, local Zhejiang banks, and the county governments will serve as the management agencies for principal and interest repayment of this public debt. Article 12: Bonds drawn in the lottery and matured interest coupons of this public debt may be used to pay all taxes in this province. Article 13: This public debt may be freely bought, sold, and mortgaged. It may be used as collateral when security deposits are required for official business in this province, and as a guarantee reserve for banks. Article 14: Anyone who forges or damages the credit of this public debt bonds will be punished by the judicial authorities according to law. Article 15: These regulations will take effect from the date of promulgation.

Sino-French Expedition Team

The Withdrawal of Chinese Members:

Hao Zhou Returns to Beiping to Report the Assault by French Team Members

Chinese Team Leader Chu Minyi Witnessed the Incident but Did Not Resist

On June 1st, the Sino-French expedition team was traveling to the Hayaer Matu area in northwestern Suiyuan when the leader of the vehicle convoy, a Frenchman named Mr. Bu An, began to insult Chinese team member Hao Jingsheng over a minor incident. He then severely beat him, rendering him unable to move. All the Chinese team members were extremely indignant. They decided to first send team members Zhou Baohan and Hao back to Beiping. The remaining Chinese team members, feeling helpless in the wilderness, decided to withdraw only after reaching Suzhou. Hao and Zhou traveled rapidly through the desert for thirteen days, walking over a thousand miles, and arrived in Baotou on the 14th. On the afternoon of the 15th, they safely arrived in Beiping by train. They were deeply traumatized and physically exhausted. Starting on the 16th, they visited responsible personnel from Chinese academic organizations to report the incident and discuss a response and the aftermath for the Chinese team members stranded in Gansu Province. All parties expressed outrage and offered assistance. The academic organizations were willing to help the four team members who would withdraw in Suzhou, enabling them to leave the French team and continue their westward expedition. They would then return to Beiping from Xinjiang via the Siberian Railway. Yesterday (the 17th) at 2:00 PM, Hao, Zhou, and others hosted a press conference to report the unreasonable actions of the French team members and the truth about their withdrawal. Over twenty people attended. First, the injured team member Hao Jingsheng recounted the facts of his injury, stating that since the Sino-French expedition team departed last month, the French team members had been driving and filming freely, which had drawn criticism from the public. Although they knew the French team members would be difficult to control, they reluctantly joined the expedition for academic research. After departing from Bailingmiao, the French team members resorted to all means to insult and mistreat the Chinese team members. On June 1st, when they arrived in Usunisu, he inadvertently entered the area while the French team members were filming, and was caught on film. This angered them, and they first insulted him and then beat him. Chinese team leader Mr. Chu Minyi was present and witnessed the incident, but he was afraid of the violence and did not dare to resist. Seeing that he was vulnerable and the Chinese were easy to bully, Bu An kicked him several more times before stopping. After he was insulted, the Chinese team members held a meeting to discuss a response. They believed that this was a group action and concerned the dignity of the nation. Therefore, he and Zhou Baohan secretly withdrew in the desert, while the other four team members agreed to withdraw altogether after reaching Suzhou to avoid the French team members' suspicion and potential harm on the way. Since the French team members had weapons and were extremely violent, unexpected events could occur at any time. Therefore, they had to reach a safe area before breaking away. Only Yao Xijiu and Jiao Jihua, sent by the Military and Political Departments, carried pistols. The rest were scholars who could not fight empty-handed. Moreover, the French side had ulterior motives in collaborating with the Chinese this time, so most of their team members were rough soldiers. Their claim of scientific research was deceptive. However, they were hindered by the strict supervision of the Chinese team members and could not use their tricks. They took the opportunity to vent their anger by behaving violently. They believed that the press represented public opinion and would provide considerable and strong support for this incident. Next, Zhou Baohan reported that when the team departed from Bailingmiao, the Chinese team leader and team members, fearing that the French team members would break the agreement halfway, discussed several preventive measures and made a written agreement with the French team leader Bu An: (1) The vehicle convoy must be under the command of the Chinese team leader; (2) Filming must be supervised by the Chinese side and must obtain the Chinese side's permission. Existing footage should be checked for corrections, and future footage should comply with the agreement; (3) The vehicle seats and luggage of both teams should be equally distributed, and treatment should be equal. The French side immediately responded in writing, fully accepting the agreement, and the two sides were able to proceed. Unexpectedly, this unfortunate incident occurred on June 1st. What was most unbearable when Bu An was behaving violently was that he insulted Mr. Hao, saying, "It wouldn't matter if I shot you now. It would just add to our filming material. And I am teaching you Chinese a small lesson." Such insults were truly unbearable. As for the unequal treatment along the way, such as skimping on the Chinese team members' meals, outwardly claiming equality but only giving them two or four or five pieces of dry, coarse bread each day, not allowing them to eat their fill, while secretly providing the French team members with milk, beer, coffee, sugar, and other items, showing preferential treatment, and the French team members were not polite to Mr. Chu Minyi himself. Mr. Chu did not eat meat and asked Bu An for vegetarian food, but Bu An replied to his face, "Eat it or don't, I can't prepare it for you personally." Mr. Chu had no choice but to endure it. In short, the French team members' unreasonable actions and contemptuous manner were all embarrassing. However, these were minor personal matters and need not be mentioned. But their violence and filming of bound-foot women and beggars begging for food, deliberately insulting the Chinese, were truly harmful to national dignity and could no longer be tolerated. Now that they have returned to Beiping, they are reporting the facts to everyone. As for their response: (1) Please order the governments of the Xinjiang and Gansu provinces to refuse entry to the French team members, detain the team's vehicles, and arrest the culprit Bu An; (2) Please request the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Military Affairs to revoke the passports issued to the French team members; (3) Please request the Academic Associations to cancel the cooperation between the two sides; (4) Please request the Academic Associations to maintain the aftermath of the Chinese team members withdrawing in Suzhou, and it would be best to help them leave the French team and continue to Xinjiang to complete their westward expedition; (5) Please request the government to lodge a protest with the French side and demand punishment, apology, and compensation to uphold national dignity. The meeting adjourned at 3:30 PM. Hao, Zhou, and others have drafted a memorial and circular telegram to report the truth to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Ministry of Education, and the Ministry of Military Affairs and request a serious protest. The four Chinese team members in Suzhou, Yao Xijiu, Jiao Jihua, Liu Zhen'e, and Yang Zhongjian, have decided to withdraw. Team leader Chu Minyi has also taken the same attitude. It is still unknown whether they will be able to travel west in the future. However, the team has suffered a major blow after this incident. It is feared that the French team members will not be able to continue westward. However, the outcome of the negotiations depends on the efforts of the Academic Associations. (18th) Shanxi Province

Measures for Repaying Grain and Forage Loans

Annual Interest Rate of 6%, Principal and Interest Repaid in Three Years

Temporarily Guaranteed by the Shuohukou Customs Tariff

Taiyuan Correspondence: After the provincial government meeting approved the proposal to borrow 4 million yuan in grain and forage loans from various counties to repay the advances made by the counties in southern Shanxi for stationing troops, the lack of a stipulated repayment guarantee for this loan initially caused widespread suspicion and opposition, especially from the various sectors' Disbandment Committee and the Post-War Advancement Association. Now that the two associations have learned that the provincial government has already sent personnel to various counties to urge collection, and the situation is becoming increasingly urgent, they will hold a joint meeting in the next two days to discuss effective countermeasures. The provincial government believes that the repayment guarantee measures are based on the opinions put forward by the provincial party department, and since it is a loan, it must of course be repaid. In order to reduce social opposition and facilitate the process, it has decided to temporarily use the Shuohukou customs tariff and various production taxes in Shanxi as collateral, formulate specific repayment measures, and officially announced them yesterday (the 15th) for immediate implementation. The details of the measures are as follows: (1) The fixed amount of the grain and forage loan is 4 million yuan, all in provincial currency, specifically for repaying the advances made by various counties for purchasing grain and forage for friendly troops before the end of May of the 20th year of the Republic of China, and shall not be used for other purposes. (2) The aforementioned loan is temporarily guaranteed by the Shuohukou customs tariff and various production taxes in Shanxi. Once the back pay owed to the various armies is received from the central government, it will be repaid immediately. If it is not received, the principal and interest will be repaid in installments from the designated tax revenue. (3) The annual interest rate of the loan is 6%, starting from the day after it is delivered to the provincial treasury. (4) The county governments shall issue receipts upon receiving the loan. When submitting the loan, they shall compile a detailed roster of the names and amounts and submit it to the provincial government's finance department for verification and issuance of loan certificates. (5) For the aforementioned loan, only interest will be paid before the end of June of the 21st year of the Republic of China. Starting from July of the 21st year, principal and interest will be repaid once every six months, and the principal and interest will be repaid in three years. The dates for repaying principal and interest are June and December each year. The accrued interest before the end of June of the 20th year will be paid together with the first installment of interest. (6) Counties that have advanced funds for grain and forage for friendly troops are allowed to retain this loan to offset their advances, but only if they have been approved. The retention of the loan shall be reported in a special report, and the date of approval by the provincial government shall be the date of delivery to the provincial treasury. (7) The Shanxi Provincial Bank is designated as the agency for repaying principal and interest for the aforementioned loan. (8) These measures shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Business Tax in Guangdong Province

Merchants Demand Changes to the Standards for Shop Size and Employees

Since the abolition of the likin tax in Guangdong Province recently, various new taxes have not yet been levied, and recent expenses have been enormous. After the new finance chief Lin Yungaishang assumed office, he found that the finances of Guangdong Province were already depleted. How could he cope with such a large military expenditure? He found that the former finance director Fan Qiwu had already completed the planning for the business tax, but it was interrupted due to the political changes. Now, in order to remedy the current emergency expenditure, he had no choice but to continue the preparations. Therefore, Lin appointed his secretary Mai Tang as the director of the business tax office, specializing in handling the matter. The office began operating on the 11th, and the measures followed those set by the previous director. Tax bureaus were set up in various counties and cities, and the tax collectors who had passed the examination were also recruited separately. However, there is still a major obstacle to starting this tax, namely the opposition of the chamber of commerce to the tax standards. The finance department recently sent a letter to the chamber of commerce, asking the chamber of commerce to contribute opinions in order to improve and facilitate the process. The letter stated that the regulations on the business tax in the province had been reviewed and resolved by the Guangdong Provincial Government's Provincial Affairs Meeting and forwarded to the Ministry of Finance for record. After the abolition of the likin tax in the province, the monthly shortfall was more than 500,000 yuan. Currently, the military situation is urgent, and military expenditures are enormous. It is urgent to implement the business tax to compensate and meet the urgent needs. The previous director Fan had published the proposed regulations in various newspapers when preparing for this business tax. Later, according to requests for improvement from various merchants, he convened meetings for detailed explanations. More than a month has passed, and the merchants should have understood and comprehended the good intentions of the authorities in implementing the business tax and the perfection of the meanings of the various articles. In order to consider the merchants' situation, the Chamber of Commerce is requested to gather opinions from various merchants by the 18th of this month and propose measures that the Chamber of Commerce deems feasible, and urgently send them to the district office for review and handling. Please do not delay. The chamber of commerce has been collecting opinions from various industries in recent days. Most of them believe that the standards for shop size and employees used by the former finance director Fan as the basis for taxation hinder the development of the commercial future and violate the original intent of the business tax. There are thirty industries that advocate abolishing this standard. According to news from the finance department yesterday, the authorities intend to abolish the standards for shop size and employees. The reason is that the authorities are eager to raise funds and have to slightly accommodate the merchants' requests in order to implement the tax as soon as possible. (June 15th)

Fan Shisheng Reports the Suppression of Bandit He

Kuang Jixun Flees Back to Qiliping

Hankou Correspondence: After the bandit He Long's troops in western Hubei fled into Junxian and Yunxian, they occupied important passes such as Wudang Mountain, Yuanheguan, and Taihe Mountain, hoping to prolong their lives. After being pursued and suppressed by Fan Shisheng's 51st Division, from the 11th to the 14th of this month, all the areas occupied by the bandits were completely recovered. He led the remaining bandits to flee southwest. Fan Shisheng telegraphed yesterday to report on the suppression of He's bandits: "According to the telegrams from the heads of our division's Wang and Xie regiments, after our troops defeated He's bandits at Sunjiawan Laoying Palace on the 9th, the bandits immediately built fortifications in the Wudang Mountain and Yuanheguan area. This morning, our army again launched an attack. The Tan regiment advanced towards Juzi Tooth, and part of the Wang regiment and Li battalion advanced fiercely from the south, while the rest took a encircling position from the left wing. They engaged the bandits at Yuhuangding. Our army launched a brave assault, and at the same time, the artillery company also bombarded the bandit positions fiercely. After four hours of fierce fighting, they occupied the important and heavily fortified areas of Yuhuangding, Huilongguan, and Mozhenjing. The bandits retreated to Taizipo and resisted again. Fortunately, the officers and soldiers of the government army fought bravely, and Taizipo was occupied on that day. The bandits retreated again to Caishenmiao and Ziyungong, relying on the danger of the Shibapan and Caishenmiao to resist stubbornly. We followed up and pursued them on the day, and the bandits were unable to support themselves. Our army took advantage of the victory to pursue them directly and occupied Shibapan Wudang Mountain again. The bandits fled to Taihe Mountain. On the day, we led our troops to pursue and suppress them. The bandits still resisted relying on the danger, but they eventually ran out of ammunition and exhausted their skills and fled in the southwest direction. Our army completely recovered Taihe Mountain. It was found that the bandits were from the 7th and 8th divisions and a training regiment, with about 10,000 people and about 4,000 to 5,000 guns. In this battle, the bandit troops suffered more than 1,000 casualties, and more than 200 male and female red bandits and wounded soldiers were captured, and dozens of guns, more than 20 mules and horses, and more than 500 dan of grain were seized. Our army also suffered more than 40 casualties of officers and soldiers. The bandits were severely damaged and fled at the sound of the wind. We ordered the local teams to intercept them everywhere, and it will not be difficult to eliminate them. Respectfully reported, Fan Shisheng." As for the bandits along the Yangtze River in western Hubei, after being encircled and suppressed by Xu Yuanquan's troops, they have been largely pacified. It is now heard that Liu Xiang will also serve as the Director-General of Bandit Suppression in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River in order to command the search and suppression of the remaining bandits.

Bandit Kuang Jixun's troops, occupying the Hekou Town on the border of Huang'an and Huangpi, were defeated by Xiao Zhichu's troops. After recovering Hekou, the bandits fled to their old nest in Qiliping. In order to completely eliminate them, the Wuhan Garrison Command ordered Ji Hongchang to send a team to join Xiao's division in suppressing them. Ji left Xinyang by car on the 19th and arrived in Hankou. Xiao also arrived in Hankou from Huang'an on the same day. After visiting Director He for instructions, he will return to the defense line to supervise the suppression. (June 19th)

Northern Anhui

Giant Bandit Zhou Hanzi Arrested in Shandong

Bandit Zhou's Right Leg Is Broken, He Only Has a Prosthetic Leg

But After Being Captured, He Actually Jumped Out of the Car Window to Escape

The Police Bravely Tracked Him Down and Brought Him Back

Xuzhou Correspondence: Zhou Hanzi, a giant bandit who roamed the three provinces of Jiangsu, Henan, and Anhui, once led more than a thousand bandits to occupy the area of Xiaoxian, Suxian, and Yongcheng, robbing, kidnapping, burning, and committing all kinds of evil. The people hated him to the bone. Xiaoxian offered a reward of 2,000 yuan for his arrest, and Suxian offered a reward of 1,500 yuan for his arrest, but neither was successful. On the 14th of this month, Wang Xinlan, the magistrate of Suxian, heard that Bandit Zhou was hiding in Li Yinzhai, which belongs to Wenshang County, northwest of Jining. He immediately sent Yu Chengyi, the second squad leader of the eighth district guard group stationed in Suixikou, with eleven armed policemen and four plainclothes policemen, each carrying guns and ammunition, to depart from Suixikou. They arrived in Jining on the 16th. On the morning of the 17th, the Jining County Government sent ten policemen to assist. They took a car to Li Yinzhai. The giant bandit was captured while he was smoking opium. Two female hostages were also found, one was Zhang Yan, about twenty years old, and the other was the virgin Xu, about twenty years old. In the afternoon at 4 pm, they were taken back to Jining together and transferred to Yanzhou. When taking the Pingpu train south, at 9 pm the military drove south from Hanzhuang Station for about fifteen miles, the giant bandit suddenly jumped out of the window, and the guards also jumped down. Eight more policemen got out of the car and tracked him down. After about a mile, they captured the bandit back and took another train south. On the morning of the 18th, the car arrived in Xuzhou. The police and Bandit Zhou stayed at the Daguan Hotel. The reporter went to visit and saw that the bandit's right leg was broken, and he only had a leather prosthetic leg. The police were afraid that the bandit would escape, so they took off his prosthetic leg. The bandit was smoking opium, and a policeman was massaging his back. After a short rest, the bandit cursed incessantly. Squad Leader Yu told the reporter that he planned to take a car to Suixikou tomorrow morning and then go to Suxian. It is heard that the thick man once served as the commander of the regiment under Sun Jingtai, who was previously defeated in the 27th division.

The Jiangsu Provincial Party Department Presents a Document to the Central Government

Opposing the Establishment of a Narcotics Suppression Bureau

It has recently been reported that "the government has decided to establish a National Narcotics Suppression Bureau, which will be directly under the Ministry of Finance. Narcotics Suppression Bureaus will be established in each province, subordinate to the National Narcotics Suppression Bureau. Li Hongji has been appointed by the Ministry of Finance as the Director." It is also reported that people are discussing that the government's policy on narcotics suppression will change direction. The association is alarmed by the severe harm of opium and is pained by the spread of narcotics. After hearing about it, we are horrified and saddened and feel sorry for our party. Our country was oppressed by imperialism, starting with the Opium War. Unfortunately, we failed, and we had to cede land and pay reparations to form an alliance under the city. At that time, the people's hearts were not dead, and they still knew to wipe out the shame and take revenge. When the Republic of China was established, the power of the country was stolen by warlords. These warlords only knew how to fight for land and profit and exploit the people. But they still did not dare to defy the world and openly advocate abolishing the ban on opium and using opium tax as a source of income. When our party unified the country and raised the banner of the Three People's Principles to save the country and the people, the people of the country followed suit. The reason is that justice lies in the hearts of the people. Our Party Leader deeply knew the harm of opium, which could destroy the country and exterminate the race. In 1924, he issued an anti-narcotics statement, saying that "the opium business can absolutely not coexist with the national government granted power by the people." He also said, "Anyone who advocates that the law allows the opium business and the customs allow opium to be imported to fill the coffers is a temporary expedient and an enemy of public opinion. If the responsible government agency lowers its flag and ceases to suppress opium for its own convenience, no matter how long or short, it is an act of treason." The last words are there, and we must not ignore them. In order to thoroughly ban narcotics, our party followed the Party Leader's last words and established a Narcotics Suppression Committee by the national government to take charge of the matter. The people of the country said that China's narcotics could be completely eradicated from now on. The revolutionary government hates evil like an enemy and cannot be compared with the Manchu Qing government and the era of warlords. It will be able to thoroughly declare war to the end against the evil opium drug. But soon there was talk of the opium monopoly, which spread at home and abroad. The association was deeply afraid that this kind of rumor would damage the prestige of our party's government. It had previously requested the Council to announce the truth in order to refute the rumors. It was later ordered to reply that the National Government had replied, "Banning opium is the government's established policy and is being implemented. There is no such thing as a monopoly." The report was published, and the doubts were dispelled. When the National Assembly opened, Chairman Chiang reiterated the government's anti-narcotics stance to all national representatives, and the people were happy. Now, not long after, there is the ominous news that the government has decided to establish a Narcotics Suppression Bureau directly under the Ministry of Finance, which is spreading in society. This further confirms that the previous talk of a monopoly was not entirely unfounded. It is not impossible for the government to ban opium and set up a special narcotics suppression agency. However, it is obvious that the intention of subordinating the narcotics suppression agency to the Ministry of Finance is self-evident. The government already has a National Narcotics Suppression Committee to handle narcotics suppression matters. Why is there another such incongruous Narcotics Suppression Bureau subordinate to the Ministry of Finance? This is truly confusing. Our country has suffered from opium for decades, and the pain is deep and unbearable. Therefore, the people of the country regard opium as a snake or scorpion and advocate a thorough ban. Even women and children know that the method of using opium tax to fill the coffers is not feasible. Moreover, today's revolutionary government bears the mission of realizing the party's agenda. How can it lower its flag and cease to suppress opium, which is unanimously hated by the people of the country, and use it for profit? The association deeply wishes that the news reported is not true. However, the people are talking about it, and it is not entirely unfounded. If unfortunately this news becomes a reality, not only will the government's prestige be completely lost, but what will our party say to the people's accusations and silence the reactionaries? The association is respectfully mindful of the Party Leader's earnest words and sees the rampant narcotics in the country. We dare not speak out what we fear. Therefore, we specially present this document for review and request the National Government to pay close attention and not be misled by villains, lest we leave behind regret. We await orders with trepidation. Respectfully presented to the Central Executive Committee, the Jiangsu Provincial Party Affairs Consolidation Committee,

Suzhou

Collection of Housing Tax for Self-Defense Expenses: The city area business community self-defense force was established last winter. Later, due to the establishment of the Zhi Xiang District Office, it was planned to reorganize the business community self-defense force into a protection corps. However, at that time, due to the lack of funds, the three district chiefs of the city and suburbs proposed a plan to collect 15% of the actual housing tax collected from the housing tax to subsidize the expenses. The county government then submitted it to the Finance Department for approval. Yesterday, the county government received a letter from Chairman Ye of the provincial government, stating that the standard for this collection plan and the month from which it should be collected should be clarified by the county government for approval.

District Chief Punished for Temple Fair Incident: In Xiangcheng Town, under the jurisdiction of the county, a temple fair was held on March 28th. A tragic incident occurred where a member of the local militia shot and killed a villager. After the incident, the district chief of the district, Zou Zhaolin, submitted a report to the county government, which was then forwarded to the Department of Civil Affairs for instructions. Yesterday, the county government received instructions from the Department of Civil Affairs, stating that holding temple fairs was generally prohibited. This time, the district chief did not strictly prohibit it beforehand, which was undeniable. The district chief should be given appropriate punishment to serve as a warning, and the county should re-investigate the details of the incident and report it to the department for review.

Wuxi

Factory Guard Beats Food Delivery Man to Death: Li Ashou, a resident of Hou Yang Cang outside the South Gate, went to the Yongyu Silk Factory to deliver food at noon the day before yesterday. He suddenly had a quarrel with a factory guard, which led to a physical altercation. Ashou was severely injured after being beaten. The factory guard sent Zhi Shou to the Third Public Security Bureau for investigation. The patrol officer on duty saw that Li's injuries were very serious and released him immediately. Unexpectedly, he died of his injuries after returning home. His family is now in negotiations with the guard, and it is said that Li Ashou was a carpenter at the Yeqin Yarn Factory, 35 years old, and his family is very poor.

Degenerate Man Commits Suicide by Drowning: Yang Guangzhong, a resident of Xiaolou Lane in the city, was 31 years old. His wife, Lu, passed away three years ago. Yang used to work at the Dafeng Rice Shop outside the North Gate, but he has now quit and is unemployed at home. He also smokes opium, and his life is extremely degenerate. He has been very short of money recently. Yang suddenly suffered from mental illness, appearing delirious and crazy. He has repeatedly attempted suicide by drowning, but he was rescued. After dinner the day before yesterday, Yang Guangzhong went out and did not return. The next morning, Yang's body was found in the Ran Jing Bridge River. The head of the Tu, Shao Jinji, reported it to the County Court and requested an autopsy. The Prosecutor's Office reported it, and Prosecutor Du, along with Coroner Shen and bailiffs, performed an autopsy according to the law. The autopsy revealed that Yang Guangzhong had no injuries on his body and had died by drowning. There was no other cause of death. He instructed the sister of the deceased, Zheng Yang, to prepare a coffin for burial.

Summary of Resolutions of the County Party Rectification Conference: The County Party Rectification Conference held its 118th committee meeting yesterday. The chairman, Hu Nianqian, made the following decisions on key cases: (1) The Zouqu Tea Garden Industry Guild reported that Inspector Wang of the County Public Security Bureau, together with Director Cao of the Eighth Branch, led a detective team and detectives, under the false pretense of arresting gamblers, entered a residence, arbitrarily searched and seized silver dollars, abused their power, and harmed the people. The meeting decided that after investigation, it was confirmed that Detective You Ada and others of the Eighth Branch had improper behavior, and the Public Security Bureau should be requested to investigate and punish them. (2) Citizens Guo Chuqing and 58 others reported that Wang Wenzao used private torture to force confessions, falsely accused innocent people of theft, clarified the truth about Wang Agou being falsely accused, and jointly requested that justice be upheld to appease the people. The meeting decided to transfer the case to the County Court for fair and lawful handling. (3) Citizens Zheng Yongquan and 45 others reported that Shi Baoquan bribed Detective Captain Xue Furui to falsely accuse Zheng Shunfu of theft, detailed Shunfu's usual kindness, jointly presented evidence, and requested redress. The meeting decided to forward the letter to the Public Security Bureau for investigation. (4) Citizens Jiang Axian, Jiang Fengbao, etc., reported that Chen Fengxu falsely accused them and imprisoned them innocently without release or trial, and requested immediate release to clear their grievances. The meeting decided to forward the letter to the County Court for investigation. (5) The Fifth District Party Department reported that Tang Bingquan, the district chief of the Fifteenth District, was incompetent and delayed important official business. The meeting decided to forward the letter to the County Government for investigation. (6) Tao Nianzu, Zhao Kui, and 223 other shops reported that the Qishuyan Power Plant published a notice canceling electricity price discounts, and jointly requested that the Provincial Party Department be forwarded to the Construction Committee to comply with public opinion, reduce the burden, and alleviate the people's difficulties. The meeting decided to forward the letter to the Construction Committee for investigation. (7) The First District Party Department reported that Pu Shuying was building illegally and requested that the Construction Bureau be forwarded to order a stop. The meeting decided to forward the letter to the Construction Bureau for investigation. (8) The First District Party Department requested that the County Government be consulted to strictly prevent unscrupulous merchants from exporting rice overseas. The meeting decided that a solution had already been discussed at the Third County Representative Assembly and instructed them to be informed. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Zhenjiang

Liu Kebi and Others Appeal Embezzlement and Extortion Case: Liu Kebi, the dismissed patrol captain of the Public Security Bureau's bicycle team, led three policemen, Man Yaoting, Cui Qinghe, and Li Fusheng, to Paiwan on March 27th to patrol. They privately investigated Yang Shan's family for opium lamps, hoping to extort money. The case was exposed, and they were dismissed and transferred to the court. After investigation, they were prosecuted and sentenced to six months of imprisonment and a fine of 60 yuan. It is reported that Liu Kebi and others were dissatisfied with the judgment and immediately filed an appeal. It was approved and forwarded to the High Court. The High Court ordered the Zhenjiang Court to order the police to bring Liu and the other three to Suzhou for questioning. After receiving the order, the Prosecutor's Office interrogated Liu Kebi, Man Yaoting, Li Fusheng, and Cui Qinghe in court yesterday and prepared a document to appoint He Qingzhou and Zheng Hua to escort Liu and others to Suzhou to appear in court.

Liyang Corruption Case Transferred to Court: The second corruption case in the Liyang Finance Bureau has attracted much attention from the public. The Jiangsu Provincial Party Rectification Committee believes that the case involves public officials' dereliction of duty and embezzlement, and they should be punished according to the law to warn against greed. It has sent a letter to the Provincial Government requesting that the case be transferred to the court for handling as soon as possible. It is reported that the Provincial Government replied to the committee yesterday that it has decided to transfer the case to the court for trial today.

Temporary End to Conscription for Road Construction: The Provincial Construction Department stated that the conscription for road construction in the province had been ordered to be implemented, and all counties had complied. However, now that the busy farming season has arrived, the conscription for road construction in all counties, except for those specifically approved, should be temporarily ended, regardless of whether they have been completed or not. The unfinished parts should be continued after the autumn harvest this year. Therefore, a report form for the end of conscription for road construction in this term has been specially formulated, and all counties are instructed to fill it in accurately and in detail according to the items listed in the form within ten days of receiving the document and submit it to the department for verification.

Yangzhou

Unfortunate Marriage Ends in Suicide by Hanging: Wang Enhao, the son of the late former provincial assembly member Wang Youyun, from Jinyu Lane in the city, was fond of pleasure. He married Zhang Wuchang, the niece of Zhang Yunsu, the director of the county relief home. Because Wang found Zhang to be too assertive, he deeply resented her. Later, Enhao met a woman surnamed Zhou and tried to get Zhang to leave. So he encouraged Zhang to study. Zhang dropped out of school last month due to illness and returned home. Enhao was furious when he saw her, saying that she had no ambition to study, and proposed divorce terms to the Zhang family. But the Zhang family was an old scholarly family and refused to accept the word "divorce." As a result, Wang's feelings for his wife worsened, and he abused her every day. Zhang Wuchang knew that she could not save Enhao's heart, so she hanged herself yesterday. After hearing the news, the Zhang family immediately reported it to the court. The prosecutor originally planned to come to the scene today to examine the body, but Wang Enhao begged someone to mediate. In addition to doubling the coffin and clothing and providing everything needed for the requiem mass, he also offered one hundred yuan to Director Zhang to use for charity. It is now reported that the woman's family has agreed to the request and has requested the court today (19th) to exempt the examination, and the case may be concluded in this way.

Robbers Kidnap and Injure People: Li Jinyu (also known as San Hao Bozi), a villager from Lijiayu in the southern countryside of Xiannv Town, was raided by a dozen robbers. Li's son and daughter-in-law were injured by the robbers' knives because they cried for help, and a four-year-old child was kidnapped. The Tang Laibin family in Tangjiazhuang, a few miles away from the town, was also robbed, suffering heavy losses. The victims reported the incidents yesterday (19th) for investigation and arrest.

The Truth About the Wuchang Steamer Being Searched in Tong: According to the British Consul, the Wuchang steamer was searched by soldiers on the Nantong River on March 15th, and 300 bags of opium were seized. He requested an investigation. The County Government was ordered to conduct a fair investigation and reply. After receiving the order, County Magistrate Zhang ordered the County Public Security Bureau to conduct a detailed investigation. On the 19th, Director Zhang of the Public Security Bureau reported to the County Government that, according to Yao Port residents, a small chestnut-yellow coal-burning steamer arrived at the Yao Port River at dusk on March 15th and anchored. There were about 30 or 40 gray-uniformed armed soldiers with armbands on board. Because it was anchored on the river, it was quite far away, and it was not known which army it was. When it was about to dawn at night, the Wuchang steamer arrived at Yao Port from upstream and anchored to unload passengers. The soldiers on the small steamer boarded the steamer and searched it, and then sailed upstream at dawn. The reason for the search was unknown because it was on the river.

Finance Bureau Clears Outstanding Education Fees: The former Director of the Finance Bureau, Fu Tong, owed more than 6,000 yuan in outstanding education fees. On the 19th, the County Government received an order from the Education Funds Management Office, stating that the former Director Fu had disregarded the province's educational needs and had not paid the money despite repeated reminders. Since the money had been withheld, the County Government should supervise him to seriously clear it and wait for the results of the consultation before appointing someone responsible for paying it back in a reliable manner, and then report it to the office for approval before the case can be closed. After receiving the order, County Magistrate Zhang ordered Fu Tong to comply.

Letter Received

Letter from the Bureau of Ceremonies, Military Council of the National Government

Dear Sir/Madam, We recently read a news article in your newspaper on the 18th entitled "Government Entrusts Various Presidents to Hold Inauguration Ceremonies Tomorrow Morning," which stated that the Bureau of Ceremonies had notified various agencies yesterday to send personnel to attend the ceremony. After investigation, this Bureau has not issued the above notification. We hereby request a correction. We hope you will investigate and handle this matter. Sincerely, Bureau of Ceremonies, Military Council of the National Government, 19th.

Education News

Important News

National Implementation of Improved

Primary Teacher Treatment Measures

After the National Assembly passed the principle of improving the treatment of primary school teachers, the Government and the Executive Yuan recently ordered the Ministry of Education to handle it. The Ministry of Education ordered the provinces and cities to quickly formulate measures to improve treatment based on the local living conditions and submit them to the Ministry for record. The order stated that the Executive Yuan's Order No. 2810 stated that the National Government Civil Service Office's Letter No. 4455 stated that the National Assembly Secretariat's letter stated that the proposal to improve the treatment of primary school teachers to improve education efficiency proposed by Representative Ma Yinbing and others had been approved in principle by the eighth meeting of the National Assembly and submitted to the government for consideration. Please check and submit it for review. After the proposal was submitted to the twenty-second meeting of the National Government, it was decided to submit it to the Executive Yuan for consideration. Please record the case and copy the original document for compliance and handling. Accordingly, the original document is copied and issued to the relevant department for compliance and handling.

- Proposal to Improve Primary School Teacher Treatment to Increase Education Efficiency

Reason: Education is the foundation of a nation, and primary education is the basic training of citizens. Therefore, the responsibility of primary school teachers is extremely important. Given the heavy responsibility, their treatment should enable them to maintain an appropriate standard of living and serve the country with peace of mind. However, the treatment in all sectors is the thinnest in the education sector, and the treatment of primary school teachers is the lowest in the education sector. Taking Jiangsu Province as an example, the monthly salary of primary school teachers in most areas is less than ten yuan. Jiangsu Province is known as a developed education area, and the treatment is still like this, so the situation in other provinces can be imagined. Primary school teachers' annual income is not enough for their needs, not enough for savings, and even unable to maintain their personal lives. There is nothing more unfair in the world than this. In recent years, the cost of living has increased day by day, and the salary of primary school teachers should also be appropriately increased in proportion. Moreover, education is a specialized profession that must be undertaken by trained and experienced personnel. If the salary is meager and insufficient to support them, trained and experienced personnel will inevitably seek other livelihoods and leave education. As a result, those with little training and experience who are literate will muddle along, and the future of education will fall into a tragic situation. Even if those who are trained and experienced are forced to serve, they will inevitably engage in perfunctory work and fail to fulfill their duties, which will reduce education efficiency. Therefore, at this time of popularizing education, in order to enable primary school teachers to serve with peace of mind and fulfill their responsibilities to increase education efficiency, the only way is to improve treatment. A plan is proposed for public decision.

Measures: (1) Improve the treatment of primary school teachers according to the current social living standards to ensure that the salary of primary school teachers can maintain a minimum standard of living. The specific measures shall be formulated by the education authorities of each province and city and submitted to the National Government for implementation. (2) Stipulate the maximum salary for primary school teachers based on the teacher's education, experience, and performance, and implement annual salary increases until the maximum amount is reached. The specific measures shall be formulated by the education authorities of each province and city and submitted to the National Government for implementation. Proposers: Ma Yinbing, Huang Yuren, Gao Bozhen, and 55 others.

Memorial for Miss Mary Elizabeth Wood

- A Pioneer of Chinese Libraries -

Memorial Service Held in Wuchang on June 13th

The Wuchang education community and libraries held a memorial service for Miss Mary Elizabeth Wood, an American pioneer of Chinese libraries, at the Boone Library on June 13th. Over 600 people attended.

Brief Biography Miss Wood was born in the United States. In 1900, the Boxer Rebellion shocked the world. Miss Wood came to China alone to visit her younger brother and stayed in Wuchang to teach at Boone University. Miss Wood witnessed that the weakness of our country was due to the backwardness of culture. To promote culture and develop people's wisdom, the most important tool should be libraries. Therefore, she made a grand vow to raise funds and build the magnificent Boone Library in Wuchang in 1910, which was the beginning of public libraries in our country. Subsequently, more than 900 public libraries have been established in various provinces. The contribution of Miss Wood cannot be ignored. She also subsidized students to study library science in the United States and founded the Boone Library School in 1920. More than 70 graduates have served in libraries at home and abroad. Miss Wood went to the United States twice. The first time was to lobby the US government and members of the Senate and House of Representatives to return the Boxer Indemnity for Chinese cultural and educational undertakings. In recent years, our country has had a so-called Cultural and Educational Fund, and Miss Wood played an important role in it.

Total High School Credits: 160

Junior High School Curriculum Divided into Two Groups in the Third Year

One Group for Higher Education, One Group Specifically for Vocational Training

Elementary School Arithmetic: Games in First Grade, Symbols Taught Starting in Second Grade

No Major Revisions to National Language, Definite Scope of Stories Includes Fairy Tales and Narratives

- First Meeting of the Curriculum Standards and Equipment Committee for Primary and Secondary Schools Concludes, to Reconvene in Mid-July -

Nanjing, 20th The primary and secondary school groups of the Curriculum Standards and Equipment Committee for Primary and Secondary Schools continued to meet yesterday to discuss the following:

Secondary School Group

The Secondary School Group resolved that the junior high school curriculum should be divided into two groups starting in the third year. One group is specifically for higher education, and its academic distribution follows the credit table resolved the previous day. The other group is specifically for vocational preparation, with an additional 17 to 20 credits of elective vocational subjects (the elective subjects will be drafted by another committee for further discussion). English will be reduced by 10 credits, and manual labor will be reduced by 3 credits. It may also be extended for one year to specifically study vocational subjects. Regarding the senior high school curriculum, it was resolved that: (1) The total number of credits for senior high school is 160, including military training and elective subjects. The double credits for each subject, English, were changed to 30 credits, domestic and foreign geography were changed to 4 credits each, physics and chemistry were changed to 7 credits each, and biology was changed to 6 credits. The rest remain according to the original standards. (2) Elective courses are increased to 24 credits, accounting for 15% of the total credits. (3) Elective subjects are divided into three groups: A. Focused on liberal arts; B. Focused on science; C. Focused on vocational preparation. The subjects for the three groups of electives will be drafted by another committee.

Elementary School Group

The Elementary School Group resolved the following key points: (1) The scope of stories is defined as a general term including fairy tales and narratives. (2) The national language course is largely based on the original standards, with slight modifications to the text. The minimum graduation requirement is slightly reduced according to the original standards. The issue of elementary school vocabulary will be collected by Chen Heqin and reported to the next general meeting for further discussion. (3) The social studies course will combine history, geography, and civic knowledge and will not divide them into separate categories. In the fifth and sixth grades, it will be changed to a more concrete form. Public health materials will be incorporated into health. (4) Natural science will incorporate health knowledge and skills into health. The rest are largely based on the original standards, but the minimum graduation requirement should be lowered and redrafted for submission to the next general meeting for discussion. (5) The arithmetic course will not teach formal arithmetic in the first grade, but will use arithmetic games as assignments. Symbols will be taught starting in the second grade. The arithmetic time for the first grade will be added to the national language course. Abacus calculation will be taught starting in the fourth grade, with 60 minutes in the fourth grade and 30 minutes each in the fifth and sixth grades. These key items will be drafted separately. (6) Work is renamed manual labor, and the commercial information item is incorporated into arithmetic. (7) Art is largely based on the original standards, and the minimum graduation requirement should be redrafted separately. (8) The health course is largely determined according to the review committee's draft and will be further considered by the original drafter before being submitted to the next general meeting for discussion. (9) Music is largely approved according to the original standards, but the minimum requirement is lowered. The complete opinions on the above resolutions must be sent to the ministry before July 5th. Both the primary and secondary school groups are scheduled to hold the second general meeting around July 15th. The official meeting minutes will be published after being compiled.

Our country's library cause relies heavily on Miss Wood's donation, guidance and promotion. Unfortunately, she became ill from overwork and died in her private residence in Wuchang on May 1st, at the age of 70. The memorial service was held in the Stuart Hall of the Boone Library in Wuchang. In the center of the auditorium hung Miss Wood's portrait, which was kind and benevolent. Around the venue hung elegiac couplets and eulogies, creating a solemn and tranquil atmosphere. At around 1:00 PM, representatives of organizations and individuals, numbering 600 to 700, arrived. Mr. Cui Younan chaired the ceremony. After offering flowers and paying respects, the chairman and Shen Zurong successively reported on Miss Wood's deeds. Director Huang of the Education Department and President Wang Shijie of Wuhan University followed with speeches, hoping that society would continue and support Miss Wood's spirit. Many bishops and other education figures spoke. Finally, telegrams of condolence received from all parties were reported, including from Foreign Minister Wang, Hu Shi, Ren Hongjun, and the American Episcopal Bishop. Those with written eulogies included Cai Yuanpei, etc. There were also donations and gifts from various parties. Finally, blessings were given and the meeting adjourned.

Vocational Education Society Holds Vocational Education Discussion

Address: Boxian Park, Zhenjiang

Scheduled to Be Held on August 1st and 2nd

The Chinese Vocational Education Society usually convenes a national vocational education discussion conference every year. This year, it is scheduled to be held at Boxian Park in Zhenjiang on August 1st and 2nd. Yesterday, a special letter was sent to various vocational education institutions to nominate representatives to attend, stating that the society usually convenes a joint discussion meeting of national vocational education institutions to discuss vocational education facilities. It has been held eight times in places such as Shanghai, Beiping, Wuchang, Nanjing, Hangzhou, and Suzhou. At the last meeting, it was tentatively decided that this year's meeting would be held in Liaoning or Beiping. Now, with the consent of the annual chairman, National Tongji University, and the support of the Jiangsu Provincial authorities, it has been decided to change this year's national vocational education discussion conference to Zhenjiang. This is because it is close to the capital and is a new provincial governance location. It is also at a time when the Ministry of Education is actively promoting vocational education. Holding the meeting there can attract attention from all parties and achieve greater results. The meeting is scheduled for August 1st and 2nd, and the venue is Boxian Park. This letter is sent to you to request that your institution nominate one to three representatives to attend as soon as possible. By July 5th, please provide detailed information on the institution's name, the representative's name, the railway or waterway starting and ending points, and the round-trip dates, so that the society can compile a list and submit it to the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Communications for approval. The society will then send a certificate for discounted train or boat tickets, so that the representatives attending the meeting can purchase tickets at the railway stations and the shipping companies under the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company with the certificate and enjoy preferential treatment. In addition to submitting concise reports on the facility's situation and the difficulties and experiences encountered, the conference will also discuss general vocational education. The society will compile implementation plans and various standard outlines for public discussion. The proposals submitted by each institution should be based on the resolutions of the last meeting, focusing on the issues of graduate employment, moral education and teaching, and women's domestic education and rural education, in order to focus the discussion and achieve satisfactory results. Please submit the proposals by July 3rd, so that they can be organized and we will be grateful.

Commercial News

Financial Silver Prices Rise in London and New York

Yesterday was the Summer Solstice. All foreign banks and the Money Trade Association were closed for the day. There were no reports on financial exchange rates. However, news from London indicated that large bars of silver all saw increases. Near and far term contracts each rose by 0.0625, both reaching 12 pence and 4.375 points. Spot trading was limited, with a small number of purchases from India. The market trended flat, but after closing, the market turned firm. American banks were inclined to buy rather than sell. News from New York also indicated that American silver prices rose by 0.125, with spot prices at 26.75 cents. The market was very firm. The Japanese-American exchange rate added one point to 49 dollars and 39 points. The British-Japanese exchange rate remained at 2 shillings and 0.0375. The British-American exchange rate fell by 0.03125 to 4 dollars, 86 cents, and 4.375 points. The American-British exchange rate added 0.1875 to 4 dollars, 86 cents, and 17/32 of a point. The British-Shanghai shilling remained at 1 shilling and 2.5 pence. Bombay spot prices increased by 5 annas to 42 rupees and 11 annas. The market rose due to reports of increases in London. A New York private telegram indicated an increase of 5/32 to 27.03125 cents.

Securities: Bond Prices Continue Strong Rise This Week

Increased by approximately 2-3 dollars compared to last week

Trading volume reached 10.6 million in five days

This week, the market was closed on Saturday for the Dragon Boat Festival. The market was only open for five days. Although the sale of long-term futures was still limited to the provision of existing products, trading became increasingly active. Recent transactions were also robust. Transactions for the 20-year customs bonds were particularly vigorous, with extremely large daily inflows and outflows. According to the daily transaction situation, Monday was the busiest day, with a total of over 26 million yuan. The other days each saw around 20 million yuan. The total turnover for the week was 10,649,500 yuan, an increase of over 1.1 million yuan compared to last week. The 20-year customs bonds accounted for 37,155,000 yuan, with 28,540,000 yuan for the June contract and 8,615,000 yuan for the July contract. Other bonds were similar to before, such as 16,910,000 yuan for the 20-year cigarette bonds, 13,755,000 yuan for the 1929 customs bonds, 12,325,000 yuan for the 1929 rehabilitation bonds, and 11,640,000 yuan for the disarmament bonds, and 11,150,000 yuan for the demobilization bonds. The remaining bonds were still quiet, such as 1,280,000 yuan for the customs bonds, 1,225,000 yuan for the Reorganization 6% bonds, and 1,250,000 yuan for the 96 public bonds. Furthermore, 5,000 yuan of the 1918 bonds were traded on the weekend. The spot market was extremely quiet, with a total transaction volume of only 17,800 yuan for the week. Each bond only saw transactions of several thousand yuan. There were no transactions for disarmament, 1929 rehabilitation, and 20-year cigarette bonds. As for the trend of various bonds this week, the market squeeze on Monday was still quite obvious. Short sellers covered their positions, and market demand continued to surge. The gap between supply and demand widened, and prices continued to rise sharply from the previous week. The June and July contracts for the 20-year cigarette bonds and the July contracts for the disarmament and 20-year customs bonds all rose to the limit price and trading was suspended. Other bonds also continued to rise by about 2-3 yuan. However, afterwards, a certain party believed that bond prices had risen significantly in recent weeks, and the market situation was still characterized by excessive demand. Therefore, they took the opportunity to sell off gradually. As a result, the market situation eased slightly, and bond prices also weakened accordingly. On Tuesday, prices fell back by about one yuan. On Wednesday, there were mixed gains and losses, with small fluctuations. On Thursday, prices continued to fall slightly by one yuan to one and a half yuan. However, on Friday, the market turned firm again. The 20-year customs bonds rose by about 2.67 yuan, and the demobilization and disarmament bonds also improved by about one yuan to one and a half yuan. The trend of the bond market is still relatively strong. However, judging from the current environment, it seems unlikely that there will be a continued large increase in the short term. As a result, compared to last week, the 20-year customs bonds rose by nearly four yuan, the 20-year cigarette bonds improved by about three and a half yuan, and the 1929 customs bonds, rehabilitation bonds, demobilization bonds, disarmament bonds, etc., also continued to rise by about two yuan. Other trends were more moderate. The statistics of the highest, lowest, and net changes in the prices of various bonds in the past five days are listed below (unit: yuan):

Cotton Yarn: American Cotton Retraces After Initial Short Covering

Yesterday, American cotton rose due to positive news from Liverpool, prompting buying by peers and short covering. Futures rose by 23-26 points, and spot prices rose by 25 points. British cotton futures fell by 6-7 points, and spot prices fell by 4 points. Egyptian cotton spot prices fell by 10 points. Indian cotton initially weakened due to profit-taking by bulls and selling by speculators, but then recovered due to positive news from Liverpool. The market closed quietly and steadily.
