Silk and Tea: Silkworm Plague Discovered in Shaoxing Summer Silkworms

Continuous Old Rain...Stuffy and Humid...Silkworm Diseases Abound

This year, farmers in various cities and towns in Shaoxing, due to the poor harvest of spring cocoons, have started raising summer silkworms earlier, and the amount of silkworms raised is no less than that of spring silkworms. Unfortunately, due to the difficulty in purchasing seeds, the local species and the foreign species are mixed for rearing. When the big batch of silkworms entered the third sleep stage, continuous moldy rain fell in recent days, and the climate was stuffy and humid. Consequently, the silkworms contracted diseases due to the wet temperature. The disease is characterized by black liquid and yellow watery discharge. If the silkworm plague spreads, it will be very rapid. Instructors are currently trying to isolate and selectively discard the summer silkworms. The future is still viewed with pessimism.

Hardware Market Quiet During Dragon Boat Festival

Yesterday was the traditional Dragon Boat Festival. Hardware transactions were even quieter. The visiting merchants and local shops were all settling their accounts for the festival, so there were no additional purchases. Consequently, the market was merely decorative. Besides occasional retail sales from shops, large-scale business can be described as desolate.

Local News Two

A Record of Two Women Running Away

Zhu Sen Achieves Two Goals with One Arrow

Xu Zhaodi Cannot Evade Responsibility

Tang Xiulin Is Shameless

Tang Baoshan, the owner of the Victory Candy and Biscuit Shop at 932 Wuding Road, whose ancestral home is Ningbo, has a daughter named Xiulin, who is 29 years old and unmarried. She is good friends with Xu Zhaodi, a neighboring girl. Zhaodi is in her early twenties, beautiful and naturally flirtatious. She has long been involved with Zhu Sen, a clerk at the Hexing Foreign Goods Store at 930, whose ancestral home is Anhui. Zhu is only 22 years old and still unmarried. They have a long-standing agreement to marry each other, but Zhaodi's parents remain ignorant. Recently, they even betrothed their daughter to someone else. Both parties were greatly disappointed. Zhaodi, wanting to comfort her lover, introduced Xiulin to Zhu. They fell in love at first sight and were both satisfied. Zhaodi then took it upon herself to act as a matchmaker, repeatedly speaking on Zhu’s behalf to Tang Baoshan. Tang and Zhu lived next to each other, and Tang had long been aware of Zhu's ambiguous behavior with Zhaodi. He was unwilling to marry his daughter to Zhu, so he sternly refused. Zhu was extremely frustrated upon hearing this news, and Xiulin was even more depressed. Zhaodi was also concerned that she might marry the wrong person, since she was unable to fulfill the beautiful union between Zhu and Xiulin.

Each of the three had their own grievances, so they gathered to plot a plan to live together. Other than eloping, there was no other way. They immediately began to carry out their plan separately. Zhu Sen rented a two-story building at 431 nearby, furnished it, and asked the shop owner for a month's leave, claiming that he was returning to his hometown to visit his relatives. Xiulin, on the night of the 17th of this month, took advantage of her parents' deep sleep to steal a deposit book for 700 yuan from the Si Ming Bank, packed her bags, and

secretly went downstairs from the balcony and out through the back door. When she arrived at the entrance of the lane, Zhu and Zhaodi had already hired a car to wait for her. The three of them got into the car together and drove to Zhu's place. That night, Zhu's wish to achieve two goals with one arrow was completely satisfied. The next morning, Xiulin went to the Si Ming Bank and withdrew all the deposits. By the time Tang discovered that his daughter had run away with the money, he rushed to Si Ming to stop the payment, but it was too late. He had no choice but to report to the Hongkou Police Station, which sent Detective Liu Yongxiang to investigate Zhu's whereabouts. They were arrested at 4 PM the day before yesterday.

Zhu and the two women were still asleep at noon and hadn’t arisen. The detectives knocked for a long time before waking them up from their sweet dreams. They put on their clothes and opened the door, and were immediately taken into custody. Xiulin had 600 yuan in cash hidden on her body, and Zhu also had 112 yuan hidden on him. All of this was found during the search, and together with the baggage, they were taken to the police station and detained separately. Yesterday morning, the parents of the girl were summoned to the Special District Local Court, where Judge Feng Shide conducted the preliminary hearing. Tang Baoshan requested severe punishment for Xu Zhaodi, stating that his daughter's elopement with the money was solely due to Xu Zhaodi's instigation after failing to act as a successful matchmaker. He also stated that the deposits were his wife's personal savings, which were kept for their son, so the deposit book was under the name of his son, Xinfu. Although his daughter also had deposits, it was only 30 yuan. Tang's wife, Wang, also testified in court, recounting the details of Zhaodi acting as a matchmaker for Zhu Sen. Questioned by Xiulin, she claimed that the money was given to her by her father, so she took the deposit book with her before leaving. As for her love affair with Zhu Sen, it was entirely voluntary, and she had been repeatedly scolded by her mother for this reason, which is why she eloped. However,

she has not yet shared a bed with Zhu. She suggested that if they did not believe her, they could inspect her body. Zhaodi also testified that she had discussed renting a house with Zhu with Xiulin because she was scolded by her mother, and denied acting as a matchmaker. Zhu Sen testified that the matter was voluntary by the two women, and he did not seduce them. After questioning, Judge Feng ordered the defendants to remain in custody separately and scheduled a hearing for a later date.

Forging Official Documents to Defraud Money

Oil Factory Owner Covets Vanity

Both Documents Are Forged

A Cantonese man named Wu Wen, who claimed to be a news reporter from the Hangzhou East China News Agency, borrowed five silver dollars from his fellow townsman Li Guohua, the owner of the Huachang Oil Factory, last year in Shanghai, and then they parted ways. On April 12th of this year, Wu visited Li at the factory's distribution office at 322 North Shaanxi Road. He noticed many official licenses and approvals hanging in the reception room, and inferred that the business must be very developed. Feeling envious, he said to Li, "Your factory's business is indeed expanding daily. I suppose it has not yet been sold nationwide. Although the official commendations are already hanging all over the walls, if you could obtain approvals from the Executive Yuan of the National Government and the Shanghai Garrison Headquarters, your reputation would be even greater, and your business would naturally expand without further effort. Last year, I passed through Shanghai, and my funds were insufficient. I encountered you on the road, and you kindly helped me out of my predicament. I will never forget your kindness. If you are interested in obtaining commendation documents from the highest military and political organs such as the Executive Yuan, I have a close relative who is currently serving in the Executive Yuan, who can be of some assistance to repay your generosity in giving me money in the past." Li, hearing these words and seeing Wu's Western-style suit and leather shoes, with a spirited appearance unlike his impoverished state last year, deeply believed him. He asked if any fees were required. Wu, realizing that Li was already hooked, replied with a smile, "A small fee of one hundred yuan is sufficient." Li gave him the money as requested and entrusted the matter to him solemnly. Wu then left. A week later, he returned to Li's place, taking out a document of approval, with the seal of the Shanghai Garrison Headquarters stamped on it. He said that the approval from the Executive Yuan would also be issued soon. Li, seeing this official-looking document, was overjoyed and thanked him repeatedly. He did not distinguish whether it was genuine or fake, and immediately posted it on the wall. On April 27th, a man named Chen Yadong claimed to have been entrusted by Wu to meet with Li. After some discussion, Chen took out the document of approval No. 293 from the Executive Yuan, with the seal of Chiang Kai-shek, the concurrent head of the Yuan, stamped on it. Li was overjoyed and immediately gave Chen fifty yuan in cash and gifts worth one hundred and fifty yuan, asking Chen to pass them on to Wu as a reward. Afterwards, Li suddenly became suspicious and sent a photo of the Executive Yuan's approval to Nanjing for verification. He received a reply stating that it was forged and asking Li to investigate the forger. Wu happened to come to Li's place again the day before yesterday afternoon. Li secretly reported to the HSBC Police Station, which sent detectives to arrest Wu. Upon questioning, they learned that Wu was residing at No. 1 Rongqing Lane, Brainee Montmartre Road, French Concession. They immediately contacted the French Police Station and sent detectives to search the premises together. They found many forged envelopes from the Wujin Public Security Bureau. Yesterday morning, Wu was escorted to the Special District Local Court, where Judge Wu conducted the preliminary hearing. Wang Yaotang, the police station's lawyer, stated the circumstances of the case, requesting that Wu be punished for the crime of forging official seals under Article 235 of the Criminal Law. Li Guohua also detailed the repeated false pretenses and deceptions of the defendant. Questioned by Li, Wu claimed that all the approvals were obtained by Chen Yadong on his behalf, and he did not know whether they were genuine or fake. Judge Wu ordered the defendant to be detained and rescheduled the hearing for seven days later.

The Litigation Over Xue Chan's Estate Continues Unabated

Five More Nephews File a Lawsuit

The litigation over the estate of wealthy merchant Xue Baorun is endless. Now, five of his nephews, Xue Jinfu, Jinfu, Jinchen, Jinxiang, and Jinliang, have filed a lawsuit against Xue Baorun's wife, Sun, and his sons, Gansheng, Yansheng, Jiasheng, and Gengsheng, demanding that the defendants be ordered to hand over the estate of ten million yuan for equal distribution. However, given the enormous amount of the lawsuit, the plaintiffs are unable to pay the litigation fees and have requested assistance. The request has been approved. Yesterday morning, the Special District Local Court held a hearing. The defendants did not attend, but sent a lawyer to represent them. According to the plaintiffs' lawyer, the plaintiffs are all sons of Xue Baorun's brothers, Baogeng and Baolin. Currently, Baolin's daughter, Songyun, has also joined the lawsuit and should be approved to participate. The defendants' lawyer expressed his opinion on the approved litigation assistance, stating that the plaintiffs had previously been involved in a lawsuit with Xue Baorun in the French Concession in the seventeenth year of the Republic, which was resolved through settlement and a settlement agreement was signed. The plaintiffs' lawyer stated that although there was a lawsuit at the time, Xue Baorun claimed that his property was only over ten thousand yuan. Therefore, the plaintiffs, persuaded by relatives and friends, reached a settlement with him. However, it has now been discovered that the property is actually worth ten million, a tenfold difference, which is why they are refiling the lawsuit. Judge Xu ordered that the issue of revoking litigation assistance be decided after investigation and rescheduled the case for another hearing.

Adultery and Abduction of a Friend's Wife

Defiling Her Body and Attempting to Sell Her

Where Is Chen Xiaoxian's Conscience?

Sun Zhenyou, a native of Bengbu, went to Nanjing with his wife, Sun Ren, to seek employment. After arriving in Nanjing, Sun Ren became separated from her husband due to unfamiliarity with the place. While she was searching for him, she met Chen Xiaoxian, a fellow townsman of her husband. Upon seeing Sun Ren, who was 29 years old and of decent appearance, Chen devised a plan to lure her to Shanghai. He housed her at the Zhongxin Hotel on Jielu Road in the North Railway Station area. Sun Ren was induced to Shanghai and sexually assaulted by Chen. However, Chen had ulterior motives and took Sun Ren to the residence of a friend in Baotai, Wusong, with the intention of selling her. Liu Jingshun, a guard at the Songhu Naval Command, discovered this and detained Chen Xiaoxian and Sun Ren, sending them to the Seventh District Public Security Bureau. Zhao Zezhou, the district chief, questioned Chen Xiaoxian. Chen claimed to have served as a recruitment officer and other military positions in Bengbu and was a colleague of Sun Zhenyou. He was evasive about the rest of the story. When questioned, Sun Ren claimed that she had been lured to Shanghai and had spent three nights with Chen. Her husband was still in Nanjing. After inquiring about the details, the district chief immediately sent detectives to the hotel in Shanghai to verify the information, which was confirmed. Regardless of whether Chen Xiaoxian was a military officer or an impostor, it was proven that he had committed adultery and abduction of a married woman. He was ordered to be formally transferred to the Third Section yesterday for further investigation and processing.

Butcher

Using Electricity to Kill Rats Leads to Self-Electrocution

Unfortunately, Rubber and Other Insulating Materials Were Not Used

Yesterday at around 6 PM, Zhu Goulang, a 33-year-old butcher from Chongming who worked at Fei Xingfa's slaughterhouse on Qiujiang Road, Zhabei, caught a live rat in an iron cage in the factory shed. Zhu suddenly had a strange idea to kill the rat with electricity. He held an iron hook in his right hand and hung it on a pillar, while holding the iron cage in his left hand. He then removed the light bulb and applied electricity to the iron hook to make contact with the iron cage. Unexpectedly, the rat was not killed, and Zhu was electrocuted and fell to the ground. Zhu did not use rubber or wood to insulate himself. People discovered him but it was too late to save him, and he died. The butcher shop reported the incident to the Zhongxing Road Police Station, which in turn reported it to the Fourth District Headquarters. Today, the local guarantor will go to the Shanghai Local Court to request an autopsy.

Woman Zhu Guilin

Accusation Against Uncle and Cousin

Request for Division of Inheritance

A local woman, Zhu Guilin, represented by lawyer Yan, stated in a civil case at the French Concession Court that the plaintiff's father, Zhu Yatou, had only three daughters. The eldest daughter, Guiying, had already passed away. The second daughter, Guibao, had been adopted into another family. The plaintiff, being the third daughter, had been studying at the Xujiahui Church since childhood. All of her late father's inheritance had been managed by her paternal uncle, Zhu Shengquan, and cousins, Xin Kun and Jin Hua, without any division. Now that the plaintiff has come of age and the National Government has promulgated the right of women to inherit property, the court should order the defendants to hand over all the property for distribution. Upon being summoned yesterday, the defendants, also represented by a lawyer, argued that the first defendant, Zhu Shengquan's father, Rongzhang, the plaintiff's grandfather, had three sons. The plaintiff's father was from the eldest branch, while the defendant Shengquan was from the second branch. The third branch had two sons, namely Jin Kun and Jin Hua. All of the Zhu family's inheritance had already been divided. Zhu Yatou's property had been sold to the defendants by the plaintiff, Zhu Guilin, ten years ago for 4,000 yuan, and a deed of sale was drawn up, witnessed by Zhu Xiangong of the church. The contract is now presented for review. The plaintiff's lawyer stated that the plaintiff vehemently denies this. The money obtained at that time was for school fees, not proceeds from the sale of property. Furthermore, ten years ago, the plaintiff was still young and immature and could not have had the capacity to sell property. The court is requested to investigate carefully. Judge Gong ordered the parties to withdraw and await further summons and verification.

Guan Daming

The Truth of the Seduction and Abandonment Case Comes to Light

The case of Chen Xuanying, a 17-year-old girl from Suzhou, who was allegedly seduced and abandoned by Guan Daming, the supervisor of a leather shoe store at the Gaodi Foreign Firm, has been clarified. Guan Daming had denied the allegations in his testimony, so Prosecutor Wu specially dispatched police officer Xu Jinqing to investigate the Shenzhou Hotel yesterday. It was found that Room 204 in November last year was occupied for only one day by someone named Dai Xingyi, but it is unknown whether this was an alias used by Guan. However, an investigation of the registration book at the New Gaosheng Hotel revealed that Guan Daming indeed stayed there with a female companion for two nights, starting on December 6th, in Room 36. He was listed as an employee of the Gaodi Foreign Firm and made two phone calls. The tea server, Wu Ronglin, also testified that Guan was a Western suit-wearer. After reviewing Chen's statement, Prosecutor Wu has a clear understanding of the case. He interrogated Chen Xuanying, who stated that Guan had taken her to a movie around June last year, and they had a relationship. At that time, her father was working as an accountant for Guan. Her father has since resigned. In the afternoon, her father, Chen Youhe, turned himself in, requesting to take his daughter home. The judge had the father and daughter meet in court. They embraced and wept bitterly. The judge then told Chen Youhe that his daughter had attempted suicide in Pudong on the 12th and that he should take her back, discipline her well, and prevent her from having suicidal thoughts again. The case will be further investigated after summoning his eldest daughter to court for questioning. Chen immediately thanked the court and took his daughter home.

Breaking a Pottery Jug Scalds a Young Girl

The Tragic Situation of Miao Abaobao

Miao Abaobao, the nine-year-old daughter of Mrs. Miao Zhu of No. 5, Ping'an Lane, Chang'an Road, Zhabei, went to a hot water vendor to get water the day before yesterday. A man named Tao Changke also came to get water and collided with Abaobao. The pottery jug in Tao's hand fell to the ground and shattered, and the boiling water inside poured onto Abaobao's head, like a ritualistic ablution with a pouring vessel. Abaobao's head, face, chest, shoulders, and back were scalded. She was in extreme pain and rolled around on the ground. Her mother heard the commotion, ran out, and called the police, who arrested Tao and took him to the Second Precinct of the Fourth District. Because Abaobao's injuries were severe, she was immediately sent to the hospital for treatment. Tao was transferred to the District Court for questioning.

Using a Gas Stove Carelessly Causes a Fire

The Wang family at No. 12, Rongfu Lane, Avenue Auguste-Savinel, French Concession, had a fire at 8:45 yesterday morning due to careless use of a gas stove. The fire suddenly started and broke through the roof, with flames raging. The front building and the attic were burned down. Upon receiving the report, the fire department rushed to the scene with pump trucks and extinguished the fire by around 10 a.m.

Special Item

The Feetham Report, Volume 2 (Fourth Continuation)

Summary Translation of Parts Four and Five

Subsequently, considering item (C), based on the current situation in China, the system of local autonomy within the Public Concession, if its ultimate control is in the hands of Chinese voters, then this system will not be of any practical use. The current period of political tutelage is based on maintaining a system of governance. If one wishes to freely exercise the functions of the Chinese system of local autonomy in an important center of political activity, and in a location that is in constant contact with the Nanjing government and the Central Party Headquarters, such as Shanghai, it is incompatible with this system of governance. Even setting aside the danger of the government or the Kuomintang controlling elections, any council with a majority of Chinese representatives will obey the directives of the National Government or the Kuomintang. In times of emergency, the Chinese representatives will inevitably be unable to vote according to the free and determined opinions they hold as representatives of Chinese society, but will instead follow the will or instructions of the government or the Kuomintang. Once Chinese representatives assume the main responsibility with a majority, the existing situation of the Public Concession government will inevitably change fundamentally. I fear that the Chinese directors of the Municipal Council will not be able to enjoy a freer environment and fulfill their responsibilities as they do today. I believe that this outcome is inevitable under the system of governance implemented today. The above considers the entire situation from the possible aspect of organizing a government with local autonomy. However, there is still one point that must be noted, namely, that in general, the Chinese have no experience in the use of the representative system. Before allowing them to participate in a democratic constitutional government through public elections, they must undergo a period of political training. This is formally recognized by the National Government's existing administrative regulations and the political procedures prepared for the future. There are indeed some extremely capable Chinese residents in the Public Concession who have received higher education. However, although these Chinese are very important to the social, commercial, and educational life and the general welfare progress they can assist in, they constitute a very small minority among all the Chinese residents in the Public Concession. Moreover, many of them, for various reasons, are unwilling to participate in public affairs except for matters directly related to themselves. As far as all the Chinese residents of the Public Concession are concerned, in the past three years, only a small part has obtained some experience in so-called participation in representative government through the informal or semi-private methods of electing Chinese directors and Chinese committee members. Therefore, in any case, before engaging in reforms and entrusting the responsibility of handling most of the Public Concession's affairs based on autonomy to Chinese representatives, it seems necessary to first undergo a period of political education. Therefore, in conclusion, the answer to item (C) must also be negative. Under the existing circumstances, a Public Concession local autonomy system established in accordance with the Charter and controlled by a majority of Chinese voters cannot be of any practical use and cannot be expected to operate smoothly. The above-mentioned answers regarding items (A), (B), and (C) all strongly oppose any policy of immediate return. The reasons for their opposition are fundamental. Any major reform of the system of governance to reconcile divergent opinions will inevitably involve certain dangers and sacrifices, so it must be carefully considered. However, this is not merely a matter of avoiding the heavy and taking the light, such as temporarily reducing the administrative rate. In fact, this kind of problem concerns the fundamental danger and destruction. The report indicates that the conclusion regarding return is based on the opinions of both Chinese and foreign residents in the Public Concession, as summarized in Chapter 3. As mentioned above, the main objection of the foreign community to return is that, under the existing circumstances, return conflicts with security. On the Chinese side, the need for a transition period before return is also based on the same reason. This is what I believe. The "security" mentioned here should have a broad meaning. As mentioned above, the more detailed reasons I have put forward are based on military, legal, political, and administrative considerations, which can also be said to be included under the general heading of security. There are many aspects of security, and there are also many ways to undermine security. The report then mentions the attitudes of the Chinese and foreign communities in the Public Concession. The responsible persons on both sides of the Chinese and foreign residents in the Public Concession have four points of agreement, which I believe to be correct: (1) The existing system of governance established in accordance with the Land Regulations has not been regarded as a permanent system of governance. If certain conditions can be implemented, there will eventually be a day when the Concession will be returned. (2) When the time for return arrives, there must be a new system of governance established in accordance with the Charter issued by the National Government to replace the existing system of governance established in accordance with the Land Regulations. This Charter is based on the continued cooperation of Chinese and foreign residents, granting full local autonomy to the Public Concession, making it a separate district or part of Shanghai. (3) Before the return, there must be a transition period, followed by a system of governance established in accordance with the Charter. This can be regarded as a practical policy. (4) During this period, the affairs of the Public Concession should be handled through close cooperation between the Chinese and foreign residents of the Concession. From this point of view, opinions have been consistent on the final goal of future policy, on the need for a transition period before reaching that goal, and on what should be the basis for handling the Public Concession's affairs during this transition period. As for the incidental issues, such as the approximate length of the transition period, and how to prudently consider the advantages and disadvantages of the organizational methods established in accordance with the Land Regulations during the transition period, there is no doubt that opinions are currently divided. The report will need to discuss these opinions later. However, I do not see any real reason why a satisfactory agreement cannot be reached, whose scope is broad enough to include all points of practical importance. Once it is generally recognized that the yardstick of future policy is return, and that after return, it will be followed by a local autonomy system established in accordance with the Charter, in which both Chinese and foreign residents can participate, there is nothing unreasonable in expecting a major improvement in the environment for dealing with all issues related to the Public Concession in the future. In central locations such as Shanghai, there are often unreasonable elements on both sides that hold each other in contention. However, it is still hoped that reason and common sense can gradually prevail. I firmly believe that the thoughtful people in the Chinese community, whose true objections to the Public Concession's system of governance can be dispelled by acknowledging that the existing system is not a permanent system, and by acknowledging that the continuation of this system must be based on the close cooperation of Chinese and foreign residents, and by peacefully resolving various disputes and making general improvements in the administration, the value and effectiveness of cooperation can be seen to increase day by day. Regarding the permanent question, if the Public Concession's system of governance is not recognized as non-permanent and is not intended to be made permanent, then the existence of this system will be seen as endangering the future of the Chinese nation. Because Shanghai is extremely important in the future, but if the relevant powers and the foreign community living in Shanghai under the protection of the powers give up any claim to the current status of the Public Concession obtained under the treaty that can be regarded as permanent, and recognize the return in the sense mentioned above as the goal of their policy, and implement the return when the situation in China changes, making it a safe policy for both the Public Concession and the entire China, then all situations will fundamentally change. At that time, the foreigners and the powers will recognize that they are only temporarily holding the Public Concession in trust for the Chinese, do not demand permanent rule over the Public Concession, and acknowledge their obligation to eventually return the Public Concession to China. The fact that the foreign community can obtain such a large degree of control over the most important part of a city and the main commercial center of the country within Chinese territory is indeed created by a continuous series of historical circumstances. However, no one had foreseen this situation, and modern people are not responsible for the original cause. Because of this situation, and with the benefit of the efforts and operations of the Chinese and foreign residents in the Public Concession, a foundation can still be created that is of great value to today's China, and its latent value is even greater for the future China. According to the existing treaties and agreements, the powers and their people are holding this created foundation in trust for China. Since they are the current protectors of the Public Concession, if they hastily return the Public Concession to China before China is ready to accept the Concession and can provide protection and development, then they will have failed to fulfill their trusted responsibility. If, at present, it can be recognized that this is a trust, and the Public Concession ruling body established in accordance with the existing organizational law seeks to cooperate effectively with the Chinese directors during the period that must be passed before the return, this will not only benefit the powers and their people but also benefit China and the Chinese people, and should be sufficient to meet the wishes of the Chinese people. The Chinese people are now the beneficiaries of the Public Concession and the ultimate heirs in the future, and their interests are greater than the total interests of all foreign interests. The second question regarding return, namely, the establishment of a new system of governance to replace the old system of governance after return, has been further considered and two conclusions have been reached as follows: (1) The maintenance of the local autonomy system within the Public Concession is extremely important for the future of the Concession. I firmly believe that both the Chinese society and the foreign society within the Public Concession generally recognize this. (2) Maintaining the Public Concession as a separate unit, or including the Public Concession within the entire Shanghai and establishing a separate municipal agency, this issue involves numerous conflicting considerations. At first glance, there is a strong reason for the administrative unity of urban areas such as Shanghai. However, the principle of administrative unity, no matter how appropriate, cannot be unified into a policy that can be realized immediately, or say that complete unity is an appropriate method that must be obtained. When considering the issue of unity, the current different situations of each district must be taken into account, namely (1) the principles and methods of governance, (2) the progress of material development, and administrative standards, (3) the comparison of financial resources. After investigating all the different situations in the existing three regions, the judgment is as follows. On the one hand, the Public Concession and the French Concession, on the other hand, the Chinese municipal government, due to the fundamental difference between them, it is not possible to place the three regions under a unified administration on any basis and effectively protect and maintain the two principles of autonomy and the rule of law on which the Public Concession's system of governance is based, and be able to implement it fairly and without hindrance. Regarding the issue of the union of the Public Concession and the French Concession, the considerations required are significantly different from those required for the union of one Concession or two Concessions with the Shanghai Municipal Government. The union of the Public Concession and the French Concession has many obvious benefits. Even if there are obstacles to implementing a system of autonomy in both regions after the union, whose principles are the same as those currently in the Public Concession, it seems not impossible to overcome them. However, there is one thing that must be acknowledged, namely, that all obstacles are caused by the long history and the different and separate development trends of the past seventy years, and it is not easy to overcome them. What can be hoped for is that the relationship between the two regions in terms of public interests and public goals may become so deep that a path of agreement can be opened, and this agreement can ultimately unite the two regions on fair and mutually beneficial terms. Regarding the final union of the Public Concession, the French Concession, and the Chinese Municipal Government, the report mentions how inherent the difficulties are in any plan that seeks to organize a council within each part of the united region that exercises limited powers and is governed by a general agency. It also expresses an opinion that the more promising plan is to "establish separate autonomous systems within each municipal area, and to develop more effective cooperation among the three regions for certain common purposes, such as police and public health. After gaining experience in using this system, it may eventually be possible to establish a new officialdom to govern all of Shanghai." Issues three and four, which are related to the need for a transition period and how long this time should be, have been discussed. A general conclusion has also been made on the broad issue of return as follows: (A) Opposition to return as an immediately implemented practical policy is very strong. If return is implemented today, it will not only cause fatal damage to the "security" that business interests consider an important feature of the Public Concession's existing system of governance, but also make it impossible to effectively continue the system of local autonomy. However, in order to satisfy the wishes of the Chinese people and to enable the National Government to use its own powers to establish the Public Concession's future municipal government, the final return is a legitimate and necessary measure. After the return, the National Government will issue a Charter, granting the power of local autonomy to the Chinese and foreign residents of the Public Concession, making it a separate autonomous region or part of all of Shanghai. Therefore, this return should be regarded as the final goal of future policy. (B) Return should not be implemented before the following conditions are fulfilled: (1) The internal situation in China should improve to such an extent in terms of establishing the authority of the National Government to maintain order that the worries about having to defend the Public Concession against future civil wars, as well as other external dangers arising from local disturbances, are eliminated. (2) The meaning of the rule of law must have a solid foundation in China and must be expressed in a practical and effective manner in the various systems of the country. Constitutional government must progress to a certain time so that the National Government can use the Charter to stipulate an appropriate and lasting method based on autonomy for the future administration of the Public Concession, and ensure that the rights granted by the Charter are inviolable under a judicial system that can guarantee the independence of the courts and enable them to enforce their judgments. (3) The political situation in China must reach a degree that allows the local autonomy system to enjoy true independence within its scope of implementation, and not be subject to the National Government, or to be controlled by any party that holds privileges and occupies a prominent position, such as the Kuomintang today. (4) The Chinese community in the Public Concession must have sufficient experience in the use of the representative system so that it can assume most of the responsibility for the administration of the Public Concession and have a reasonable hope of success. (C) Before the above conditions are fully met, an extended transition period is unavoidable. Fulfilling these conditions involves a major change procedure. Chinese leaders are now engaged in this change. However, in order to create the fundamental changes required to fulfill the conditions and to test the effectiveness and durability of the changes, a considerable amount of time is required. If it is said that these two can be completed within a few years, then disappointment is to be expected. During this transition period, the Public Concession's existing system of governance established in accordance with the Land Regulations should be maintained on the basis of increased cooperation between Chinese and foreign residents. The organizational law should also be amended as needed. The so-called need is to enable the Chinese people to fully participate in the work of autonomy by prudently adding to or subtracting from the existing system and to prepare to ultimately organize a new system of governance based on the Charter issued by the National Government.

The Tea Industry Changes to New Weights and Measures

The Shanghai Tea Trade Association has complied with the order to change to new weights and measures. Yesterday, it issued a notice to its members stating: "By order of the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau: It has been found that there are many types of weights and measures in our country, with old and new mixed together, and even different cases in the same place, with mutual discrepancies. As a result, disputes arise frequently. At this time of construction, unifying weights and measures is indeed an important task. The former Ministry of Industry and Commerce convened a weights and measures conference, drafted a plan for promoting the main body, adopted the International Metric System as the standard, and established municipal auxiliary promotion in each city to formulate a unified national procedure, which was ordered by the National Government to be followed by all provinces and cities. This city has set a deadline of July 1st for the completion of unification, and has ordered all trade associations to actively prepare and order all shops in the same trade to adopt new equipment to show compliance with the law. If there is any delay or waiting and seeing, severe punishment will be imposed." Therefore, it was decided at the 17th Executive Committee meeting to recall all the one-jin copper pan scales previously issued to each shop, re-order the new system, and wait for the re-stamping before returning them separately, so that each shop can use the scales of this association as the standard. All other scales, large and small, etc., of each shop must be re-manufactured, and do not wait and see any longer. This is what is hoped. Therefore, a corresponding notice is issued, hoping you will check and handle it.

Municipal Public Works Bureau Completed

Unifying the City's Power Plants (Continued)

First Step Plan

Regarding the Pudong Electric Company again, that company's original steam turbine generator has a capacity of 750 kVA. In the 18th year of the Republic [1929], its maximum load had reached 450 kilowatts. The generator's capacity was soon to be insufficient to supply demand, and the original two boilers, with only one in operation, were not enough. Operating both boilers would leave no opportunity for replacement and cleaning, making it imperative to add new ones promptly. Furthermore, with only one generator and no backup, the situation was also considered dangerous. Given the trend of industrial development in Pudong, the company's future business progress should focus on attracting electricity users. However, electricity users require substantial power, which small-scale equipment cannot meet. Expanding equipment involves significant costs, and even if financially feasible, it is not the most economical solution. Therefore, the company was instructed to consult with the China General Edison Company [Huashang Electric Company] about power supply. However, with one company in Pudong and the other in Puxi, connecting power lines required crossing the Huangpu River. The engineering aspect was not as simple as the Zhenru-Xianghua companies purchasing power from Zhabei. Therefore, it initially caused considerable concern. It was later decided to lay two underwater cables in the Huangpu River. A power supply contract was signed on January 16th of the 19th year of the Republic [1930], agreeing that the line construction would be completed and power supply would commence within one year from the contract's signing. The power supply period was tentatively set for five years from the date of energization. The power supply capacity for the first year was limited to 800 kilowatts, increasing by 300 kilowatts each subsequent year. The electricity price was set at 3.5 silver cents per kilowatt-hour. After the contract was signed, two 5,500-volt underwater cables were laid in the Huangpu River. One ran from the Shanghai Bund pier to the northwest end of the Pudong Coal Industry Public Warehouse, and the other ran from approximately 280 meters southwest of the Shanghai Arsenal to the northwest end of the Pudong China Wharf. The work was gradually completed around October of the 19th year of the Republic [1930]. A switch room was built on a rented piece of land behind the Coal Industry Public Warehouse. After the two cables came ashore, a dedicated 5,500-volt overhead line was specially installed, running through the switch room to the company's power plant in Zhangjiabang, where electricity meters were installed to calculate charges by kilowatt-hour. Power supply commenced on March 1st of the 20th year of the Republic [1931]. However, due to the China General Edison Company's boiler installation not yet being completed, it could not supply electricity to its full capacity. Therefore, only the Yangsi area was temporarily supplied with power from China General Edison Company, while the area north of Tangqiao continued to be supplied by the company's own power generation. It was expected that all areas could be fully supplied by China General Edison Company by the end of the 20th year of the Republic [1931]. As for the Wusong Baoming Electric Company, its urban area was a small power plant in the north. Its mechanical equipment, aside from one gas generator that had long been abandoned, included two diesel generators with a combined capacity of 287 kVA. However, one of them was converted from a gas engine, inevitably reducing its capacity. In the 18th year of the Republic [1929], the maximum load had reached 200 kilowatts, and without expanding equipment, it would soon be insufficient. With the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company constructing a power plant near Junsong Bridge on Jungong Road, very close to the company's business area, connecting power lines along Jungong Road was very convenient. Therefore, in May of the 19th year of the Republic [1930], the company was instructed to consult with the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company on power purchase methods. After both parties reached an agreement through negotiation, a contract was signed on September 15th of the 19th year of the Republic [1930]. The power supply capacity was temporarily limited to 600 kilowatts, and the electricity price was also divided into basic fixed and variable portions. The basic portion was calculated at 3.1 taels of silver dollars per kilowatt of maximum power consumption per month, with appropriate adjustments based on the load factor. The variable portion was calculated at one silver cent per kilowatt-hour, with appropriate increases or decreases based on the amount of heat required per kilowatt-hour of electricity generated and the price of coal. After the contract was signed, a transformer substation was set up next to the Zhanghuabang Station on Jungong Road, serving as the point of entry for electricity from Zhabei. The company's entire electrical wiring within its business area was also thoroughly renovated due to the power supply. Subsequently, the Zhabei New Power Plant was completed and began generating electricity in December of the 19th year of the Republic [1930], and the company's aforementioned projects were also gradually completed. Therefore, starting from May 1st of the 20th year of the Republic [1931], power was supplied by Zhabei. The first step in the Bureau's plan to unify Shanghai's power plants was to stop power generation by small power plants and concentrate the city's power generation in the two major power plants in Zhabei and China General Edison Company. Currently, the Zhenru-Xianghua and Baoming companies have successively implemented purchasing power from Zhabei, and the Pudong Company has implemented purchasing power from China General Edison Company. The first step in the plan to unify power plants has been fully completed.

Fishing Boat Registration Deadline at the End of This Month

The Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau, upon receiving a telegram from the Ministry of Industry ordering the registration of all fishing boats, with a deadline of June 30th, issued a special announcement yesterday, stating: "Regarding the matter of this announcement, according to the Ministry of Industry's telegram, in accordance with Article 48 of the Fisheries Law and Article 39 of its Implementing Regulations, those who obtained fishing rights before the implementation of this law should apply for registration in accordance with the law within one year after the implementation of this law, otherwise they will be deemed to have abandoned their business. The deadline is June 30th of this year. In addition to telegraphing the Ministries of Transportation and Finance to instruct the Customs to strictly enforce the law within the prescribed time limit, we hereby instruct the Bureau to issue a public announcement and publish it in the local newspapers, ensuring that all fishing boats register within the time limit to protect their fishing rights and avoid detention." Upon receiving this, after reviewing the old and new fisheries, it is imperative to apply for registration in accordance with the law. This Bureau has repeatedly ordered compliance in the past. Now, in accordance with the aforementioned instructions, in addition to issuing separate orders, we hereby issue this urgent announcement, urging all fishermen in this city to be fully informed and diligent in complying.

Crossing the Pacific

Adventurous Boat Arrives in Shanghai

From Vancouver

The "Great Beauty Evening News" reported that yesterday (the 19th), an adventurous small boat arrived in the Huangpu River. With a gross tonnage of 258 tons and a crew of eleven, it crossed the turbulent Pacific Ocean, sailing for 28 days from Vancouver to Shanghai. When it moored in the Huangpu River, only one barrel of diesel fuel remained. Had it arrived several hours later, it would have been stranded at sea due to running out of fuel. The boat is named "Chautsena." Although its appearance now resembles a small fishing boat, it was once a maritime palace for British nobles forty years ago, and later a yacht for famous actors. It has sailed the Mediterranean and North Seas countless times. Fifty-one years ago today was the day the boat was launched. Its owner, the Marquess of Anglesey, named it "Suemai." It is said that the Marquess was a favorite of the Victorian court, doting on a London socialite. This boat was specially built for that woman to accompany him on maritime tours. Therefore, its construction was solid and its equipment magnificent, unparalleled in its time. It is said that on one occasion, the Marquess invited several friends to go on a sea tour, accompanied by the woman. Just before departure, the Marquess went ashore for business, and the boat departed as usual. Unexpectedly, it disappeared for three years without a trace. It was finally found after much searching, but the owner was nowhere to be found. It was then sold to the actress Lang Drai, who often used it for tours of the Riviera in the Mediterranean. After the actress died of illness, it was acquired by the Vancouver United Company and used as a ferry between Vancouver and Powell Island for twenty years. Currently, the equipment in the boat is completely different from its original appearance. Only a few windows, resplendent and luxurious, are remnants of fifty years ago. Secondly, there is the engine and a portion of the wheelhouse. According to the crew's opinions, it is a relic of the past. The boat's arrival in Shanghai has no fixed purpose. In the future, it may go to Southeast Asia or Mexico. It is difficult to predict, as its sole purpose is to trade goods for profit.

Children's Hygiene Movement

Meeting and Performance Yesterday

To continue at Yangshupu the day after tomorrow

Yesterday was the second day of the Children's Hygiene Movement held by the Children's Welfare Association on Xiqiu Road in Zhabei. The number of attendees was even more enthusiastic than the first day. The situation is described below.

Product Exhibition

The Children's Welfare Association's hospital was temporarily converted into an exhibition area for children's hygiene products. Participants in the exhibition included Le Tu Jing infant formula, Flying Eagle brand condensed milk, Quaker Oats, Palm Soap, Ke Ning milk powder, Shuangdao brand disinfectant, Lao Jin Yuanhang Mrs. Winslow's Soothing Syrup, Sanyou Industrial Society children's clothing, Dachunghua Celluloid Factory children's toys, etc. Many children's hygiene posters provided by the Health Education Society and the association were hung on the walls, which were very eye-catching.

Slogans

Many slogans were posted inside the general meeting area. The more important ones are listed below: (1) A child with a disability in the family means one more patient in society. (2) Young women should have knowledge of childcare. (3) Unmarried girls should pay attention to infant care knowledge. (4) Overthrow the old saying that one should marry only after learning how to raise children. (5) Children's clothes should be clean, comfortable, and appropriate for the season. (6) Infants get sick from overeating, so breastfeeding every three to four hours is enough. (7) Air and sunlight are the best supplements for infants. (8) To prevent smallpox, vaccination is necessary. (9) When sick and spitting phlegm, medication should be used to treat it; when not sick and spitting phlegm, education should be used to correct it. (10) There is no child in the world who is not good; it all depends on the education of the parents.

Hygiene Work

Yesterday, from 9:00 AM to 11:00 AM, the children's health competition was held. Including yesterday, a total of 144 children participated. Dr. Yang Suming and others examined the children's physical condition. The list of winners will be announced soon, and prizes will be awarded. From 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM, three doctors sent by the Municipal Health Bureau gave free vaccinations. Including yesterday, a total of 645 children were vaccinated. Children were given free baths, supervised by Ms. Hua, Huameijie, and others. Including yesterday, a total of 87 children were bathed.

Meeting Performance

The meeting began at 8:00 PM, featuring a children's hygiene lecture. A representative from the Municipal Health Bureau lectured on the essentials of children's hygiene. Guan Jingbo from Bingxun Guopu Stenography School volunteered to take notes. Then, the juvenile preaching group performed the Children's Welfare drama "Rescue the Children," which was very exciting and received enthusiastic applause from the audience. Students from the association's Children's Welfare Education Institute performed a hygiene drama titled "Flies and Mosquitoes," with guidance from Ms. Xu Yunru. The words were cautionary and the songs were melodious, which was well-received by the audience. Finally, a children's hygiene film was screened, attracting about 1,000 viewers, an unprecedented event in Zhabei. The meeting adjourned around 11:00 PM.

Relocation

The Children's Welfare Association initiated this children's hygiene movement, which will be held in Zhabei and Yangshupu in succession. The Zhabei event has been completed and will be held in Yangshupu in the same manner on the 23rd and 24th. Key officials of the association, including Wu Weide, Wang Guanyi, Zhang Yueru, and Chen Zhengfan, are extremely busy, and it is expected that there will be even more excitement at that time.

Yanghang Town

News After the Sealing of the Lingci Society

County Government Investigating Those Responsible

The Lingci Society organized by Chen and Zhou, residents of the West Market in Yanghang Town, First District of Baoshan County, was previously banned by the local Party branch for holding prayer meetings, promoting superstition, and extorting money. The details have been reported in various newspapers. It is now learned that the Baoshan County Party branch instructed the town Party branch yesterday, stating that the case of the Yanghang Lingci Society promoting superstition and extorting money has been forwarded to the county government for investigation. It has been approved in the reply that the First Section of the Public Security Bureau has been ordered to strictly prohibit it and to identify those responsible for punishment in accordance with the law. It is reported that those responsible for the society have fled upon hearing the news.

Chongdao Hall Extorting Money with Fake Spirits and Ghosts

If the Old Master is So Powerful, Why Doesn't He Move the Police?

Quitting Smoking is Indeed Psychological Therapy

Repeated Collection of Funds, the Purpose is Probably Nothing More Than Extorting Money

Yang Changguo and Cao Chunhua, from Jiangbei, established the Shanghai Hugujunying Branch of the Nanjing Chongdao Hall at No. 9 Nanjing Street. They used the pretense of spirit possession to treat people and extort money. Many ignorant men and women went there. Police Chief Zhu Lianfa of the responsible First District First Precinct discovered this. The day before yesterday, he went to the address and arrested Cao Chunhua, bringing him back to the precinct. During the preliminary hearing, Cao stated that he was 48 years old and that they had never been able to treat people, but relied on the secret assistance of the Old Master to relieve the people of all disasters and eliminate all kinds of strange diseases and demons, especially in quitting smoking. Anyone addicted to smoking would come to their place, first kneel and bow to the gods, then drink a cup of tea, and then have their qi circulated to expel the turbid air accumulated in their chests. They would then be asked to move around for a while, and they would inevitably vomit, as all the dirt in their chest and abdomen would be vomited out. Then, they would be asked to sit quietly, and after 48 hours, the addicts would completely lose their addiction. If they still thought about smoking afterwards, they could come to their altar. They would be given special treatment, provided with meals, and no money would be taken. They would only be allowed to donate incense money as they pleased. The money obtained from their altar would be placed in bamboo tubes. At the end of each year, the contents would be emptied and the total amount calculated. After deducting expenses, the rest would be submitted to the Nanjing General Altar for charitable purposes. They were charged with spreading rumors to confuse the public, extorting money for personal gain, and using spirit possession to treat people, which violated police regulations. They were ordered to remain in custody pending verification.

Huining Native Place Association

Pleading for the Disaster Victims of Jingdezhen and Huizhou

Submitting Three Requests to the National Government

The Huining Native Place Association in Shanghai submitted a request to the National Government regarding the post-disaster issues of the disaster victims of Jingdezhen and Huizhou: "Regarding the request to designate troops to protect merchants and travelers, establish national banks, and restore the market in order to seek post-disaster recovery and pacify the people, this association has received a letter from the Jingdezhen Huizhou Merchants Bandit Disaster Relief Committee, stating that since last year, Jingdezhen has been ravaged three times by the Red Bandits, occupied for five months, subjected to rape, looting, extortion, and arson. The devastation was even worse than the Taiping Rebellion. Jingdezhen is located in northern Jiangxi and borders our Huining counties, making it the only gateway in southern Anhui. Therefore, the number of Huizhou people living there is the largest, and the number of merchants doing business there is also the most. Unexpectedly, after the Red Bandits occupied the town, they promoted communist heresies, treating the Huizhou people even more cruelly than the other locals. What crime did the Huizhou people commit to suffer such a catastrophe? Fortunately, the National Army finally settled the situation, and the disaster victims gradually returned. However, nine out of ten houses were empty, and there was no way to make a living. Starvation and cold drove them to despair, huddling together in misery. The once-prosperous Huizhou merchants were now a picture of desolation and terror. The Huizhou people in Jingdezhen today are on the verge of death and are about to give up. However, there is still hope for recovery. It is necessary to take immediate action to save them. After repeated discussions, three measures have been proposed and requested to be forwarded to the Central Government for approval: (1) Jingdezhen has a large number of porcelain workers, but they have limited knowledge and are easily swayed by the bandits, becoming their accomplices. After the bandits leave, they are also prone to causing disturbances. Moreover, they also harbor resentment towards the Huizhou people. If there is no permanent military presence, not only will the lives and property of the Huizhou people be at risk, but the security of Huining will also be greatly affected. Therefore, it is necessary to request the Central Government to designate troops to be permanently stationed to maintain order and ensure the safety of Huining. (2) Jingdezhen has suffered three bandit disasters, and the Huizhou merchants have suffered the greatest losses. All financial assets and goods have been swept away, and the entire town is at a standstill. Even if there is a forced recovery, it will only be a facade and will inevitably lead to complete collapse. To seek fundamental relief, it is necessary to inject sufficient financial resources. Therefore, it is necessary to request the Central Government to establish national banks to replenish the market and restore commerce. (3) Tens of thousands of Huizhou merchants and unemployed workers are starving and freezing, living in despair. Cries of hunger and desolation are everywhere. It is necessary to request fellow native place associations in various ports to generously donate and widely solicit donations to achieve the effect of relief and allow them to survive. In summary, these three measures are the urgent requests of all Huizhou people in Jingdezhen. We hope that you will be mindful of the disaster victims and solicit donations for relief. Regarding the two items of designating troops and establishing banks, we earnestly request that you forward them to the Central Government for approval so that your word can carry weight and the results will be significant. The disaster victims of the entire town will be eternally grateful. According to this, the two items of stationing troops and establishing banks are the only good measures for post-disaster relief that benefit merchants and protect the people. We hereby submit this document with the facts and request your approval for prompt implementation to protect merchants and travelers and reassure the people. We are anxiously awaiting your orders."

Xuzhou Chunyuan Sorghum Sells Well in Shanghai

Xuzhou is a place that produces Sorghum. Every time the green gauze tents rise and the green rice waves, the red ears sway, and the villains often use it to hide. The abundance is known, and the people of Xu take it and brew it into sorghum liquor, which is thick and mellow, strong and fierce, and delicious to drink. It is a famous product of Xu and has been famous throughout the country since ancient times. In recent years, it has been distributed in Zhenjiang, Suzhou, Wuxi, Changzhou, Nanjing and other places, but Shanghai is still lacking. Tongju Liquor Store is the only large distillery in Xu, with branches all over the place. Now, a third distillery has been specially added to Shanghai, where Chinese and Western cultures meet, at No. 79 Xinyong'an Street in the French Concession, to promote it. It was opened for business on the 17th of this month, and the doors were crowded. The welcome of the people of Shanghai can be seen. Its quality is dense and pure, neither diluted with water like inferior goods, nor mixed with fake wine by those who are greedy for profit, which is harmful to the body and mind. It is predicted that sorghum liquor will be sold in Shanghai in the future.

Ming Yuan Intensifies Work

Since its reorganization into an entertainment venue, Ming Yuan has raised approximately 700,000 yuan in capital to bring in various forms of entertainment from Little Luzon, America, aiming for utmost novelty. Construction and renovation have been underway for over ten days. The existing workforce of 1,000 laborers is insufficient, so another 1,000 workers have been hired to accelerate the work. The swimming pool is being built day and night with utmost effort, hoping to create the most modern and scientific large swimming pool in Shanghai. The water will hold 10,000 gallons and will be disinfected and sterilized daily using a scientific purification and filtration machine, so that Shanghai residents who are tied to their duties and unable to escape to distant resorts for the summer can enjoy the blessings of coolness and comfort. The construction projects have all been thoroughly tested and carefully considered on-site by American experts, ensuring safety and stability without any drawbacks. According to internal staff, they hope that Ming Yuan can open in the shortest possible time.

The Social Affairs and Public Safety Bureaus Temporarily

Took Over the Wusong Chamber of Commerce Yesterday

Pending Review by the Ministry

The Shanghai Social Affairs and Public Safety Bureaus' takeover of the Wusong Chamber of Commerce and establishment of branch offices has already been reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now learned that at 10:00 AM yesterday, the Social Affairs Bureau dispatched representative Hu Yuqi, the Public Safety Bureau representative Jin Zhongjian, and the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce representative Luo Qinghua, to Wusong by car. They first contacted the Eighth District Party Headquarters, and then went directly to the Public Safety Seventh District. Since the Wusong Chamber of Commerce was located within the jurisdiction of the Seventh District, Director Zhang of the district accompanied them to the meeting. The standing committee members of the Chamber of Commerce, Zhang Zengjie and Zheng Shushan, received them. Representative Hu presented the takeover document for the two committee members to review. Committee Member Zheng replied that the Chamber of Commerce had previously received an instruction from the Ministry of Industry stating that the Chamber's request to continue its existence was not without reason, and that further review was pending. Therefore, regarding the takeover, it would be best to wait a while. After the Social Affairs Bureau representative read the Ministry of Industry's instruction, he replied that since there was such a situation, it was necessary to ask the bureau director for instructions. At about 1:00 PM, the situation was reported to Director Pan by long-distance telephone. Director Pan then sent a telegram instructing the Chamber of Commerce to temporarily hand over the seals and files to the bureau for safekeeping, pending a reply from the ministry, before further review. Representative Hu then informed the Chamber of Commerce of the situation. Committee Members Zheng and Zhang complied and handed over one seal that read "Seal of the Wusong Chamber of Commerce of Baoshan County, Jiangsu" and one small seal that read "Wusong Chamber of Commerce." Representative Hu accepted them. In addition, public documents and files were divided into three large packages, sealed, and affixed with seals, signed jointly by Social Affairs Bureau representative Hu Yuqi, Public Safety Bureau representative Jin Zhongjian, Shanghai Chamber of Commerce representative Luo Qinghua, and Wusong Chamber of Commerce representatives Zhang Zengjie and Zheng Shushan, to show their solemnity. After signing, they were handed over to Luo Qinghua for inventory and taken back to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce for temporary safekeeping. As for whether the Chamber of Commerce should continue to exist or be changed into a branch office, it would have to wait for the ministry's reply before further review. In addition, the Chamber of Commerce has three large cabinets of historical documents and account books, which were sealed by the Social Affairs Bureau in the Chamber of Commerce. The transfer of property and equipment was also completed, and they returned to Shanghai by car. Later, Wusong merchants were greatly shocked when they heard the news because it happened suddenly. It is said that an emergency meeting of the entire body will be convened that evening to discuss the aftermath.

Two Groups Oppose the Anti-Opium Bureau

Anti-Drug Association: The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association recently stated that the establishment of the Anti-Opium Bureau by the Ministry of Finance, implementing a method of prohibition through taxation, and the establishment of bureaus in various provinces to collect taxes, while the two-percent opium surtax, which the people have been calling for over a year, continues to exist, clearly contradicts the current anti-opium law and violates the Hague Anti-Opium Convention, the Kuomintang party platform, and Premier Sun Yat-sen's anti-drug legacy. It is recognized outside that such measures are tantamount to a disguised public sale, similar to Wu Liande's public sale proposal, and criticisms have arisen. Anti-drug organizations and local party headquarters are sending messages expressing their opposition. Serious advocacy is increasing daily. It can be seen where public opinion lies. The association is currently based on its arguments over the years and the unanimous demands of local anti-drug groups, requesting the central government to correct these methods to maintain international credibility and comfort the people's hope. According to the association, the association supports any anti-opium measures that do not contradict Premier Sun Yat-sen's anti-drug legacy. Any anti-opium measures that violate Premier Sun's legacy are opposed. Also, those outside who do not know the contents of Premier Sun Yat-sen's anti-drug legacy are asking the association for copies. The association has prepared an additional 10,000 posters of Premier Sun Yat-sen's anti-drug legacy and 100,000 copies of the full text of Premier Sun Yat-sen's anti-drug legacy. All levels of party headquarters, mass organizations, schools, and church groups can send an official letter to the association requesting copies. Five copies will be given free of charge to promote it, it is said.

Women's Temperance Association: The Chinese Women's Temperance Association, in view of the harm of opium to China, has been very active in the anti-drug movement for several years. Recently, the Ministry of Finance established the Anti-Opium Bureau, suspected of adopting a method of strict prohibition through taxation. The association absolutely opposes the above method and issued a declaration yesterday, with very strong wording, it is said.
