National Products Mall Submitted Conditions Yesterday

Reopening After Seven Conditions Are Resolved

Employees Were Still Arrested Yesterday and Released Immediately

The National Products Mall has been ordered to close by the Public Works Department for eleven days and has not yet been resolved. Yesterday, the mall's negotiation committee met and decided to submit seven conditions to the Public Works Department, and will reopen after they are resolved. The Public Works Department is scheduled to reply in writing on the 22nd. The conditions are recorded below.

Continued Negotiations On the 19th, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce convened talks between the two sides. Because it was late, the Public Works Department representative requested a postponement for further discussion. It was decided that continued reporting would take place at 3:00 PM yesterday. PWD Chief Inspector Mao Ding, West Director Brown, Chinese Director Yu Qiaqing, Yuan Liden, Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Wang Xiaolai, Xu Jiyi, and Chinese National Products Mall representatives Hong Yanbin, Ren Jinpin, Zhu Zhenhan then began the discussion. Chief Inspector Brown began by describing the Public Works Department's equipment issues for the National Products Mall. The chairman then asked a number of questions, asking for clarification. Brown then said that the engineering department would reduce the minimum requirements for the National Products Mall's equipment and would provide a written list of responses on Monday. Then, the National Products Mall representative declared to the chairman that the crux of the case now lay in the issue of responsibility for the June 9th incident. If the issue of responsibility is not determined, then nothing can be discussed. This must be solemnly declared.

Negotiation Committee The National Products Mall Negotiation Committee held a meeting at 10:00 AM yesterday, chaired by Zhang Zilian. Regarding the Public Works Department's illegal blockade of the mall and order to cease operations, it was resolved that (1) matters concerning violation of the agreement and infringement of legal rights will be handled by the government; (2) regarding its own issues, it will submit seven conditions to the Public Works Department; (3) regarding the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's continued negotiations at 3:00 PM, it will send Hong Yanbin, Ren Jinpin, and Zhu Zhenhan to attend.

Submitted Conditions The National Products Mall Negotiation Committee submitted a total of seven conditions to the Public Works Department: (1) The Public Works Department apologizes to the Chinese government, the national populace, and the mall, and publishes the apology in Chinese and Western newspapers; (2) Punish the responsible personnel who closed the mall and beat the employees; (3) Guarantee that similar incidents will not occur to all residents of the concession in the future; (4) The Public Works Department shall not interfere with the organization of all national products malls in the concession and the promotion of national goods; (5) The provisions regarding the issuance of permits and inspection of Chinese civil construction and hygiene and fire prevention equipment in the Land Regulations and Public Works Department By-laws should be amended immediately for the following purposes: (A) Residents must have the right to appeal when they deem the Public Works Department's disposition to be inappropriate or unacceptable; (B) Establish a review body for reviewing the issuance of licenses and hygiene and fire prevention equipment; (C) The upper-level body must be composed of Chinese personnel organized by the Shanghai Municipal Government-appointed Chinese taxpayers' association; (D) Any for-profit or non-profit organization set up for residents shall not be subjected to suspension or closure without prior judgment by a Chinese court; (6) Compensation for the loss of the entire mall; (7) After all the above conditions have been completely resolved, the responsible personnel of the Public Works Department shall personally open the door. The opening method and time shall be determined separately by the mall.

Zhu Zhenhan's Talk Yesterday at 6:00 PM, reporters from various newspapers spoke with Mr. Zhu Zhenhan, a member of the mall's negotiation committee. Mr. Zhu said that it was unfortunate that the mall was illegally closed by the Public Works Department on June 9. Although Chinese Director Yu Qiaqing mediated and convened talks at the Chamber of Commerce, both sides reported on the mall's renovations and layout. He believed that this was not a fundamental solution. In his opinion, this matter should clarify the responsibility for the illegal closure on June 9, and then the secondary issue of renovation can be discussed. But in studying the renovation, the various regulations set by the Public Works Department, such as the fire brigade, the engineering department, the health department, and the police, are one-sided by the Public Works Department, and whether they are proper is a very large question. This question should be noted not only by the Chinese directors in the bureau, but also by all our citizens, to study whether they are proper. Therefore, at the meeting, after the Public Works Department finished reporting, West Director Brown said that the mall and entertainment venue could be opened tomorrow if they wanted to. This was rejected, saying that the mall could not be opened until the responsibility was clarified and public and private matters were resolved.

Employee Arrests and Releases In order to make the public understand the truth about being ordered to close by the Public Works Department, the National Products Mall Negotiation Committee dispatched personnel to distribute the National Products Mall Daily. Yesterday at 4:50 PM, employee Zhang Hanchen was arrested by Western officers from the New Gate Police Station while distributing promotional materials on Nanjing Road, and was released shortly afterward. At 6:20 PM, employee Hu Zhentao was also arrested by Western officers from the New Gate Police Station. It was reported that he was also released that night.

Ministry of Industry Instruction The Ministry of Industry issued an instruction to the National Products Mall yesterday: "It is learned that the mall reported the circumstances of its closure, requesting a review and prompt negotiations to save the merchants and maintain national goods. This case was previously referred to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to file a protest and conduct serious negotiations. Now, according to the detailed report, it has been referred again to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for handling. Please be informed of this instruction."

Party Headquarters Reply The Secretariat of the Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters sent a letter to the National Products Mall yesterday: "Respected sirs, it is learned that the Shanghai Municipal Government's letter No. 2896 stated, 'It is learned that your secretariat's letter No. 2681 regarding the Public Concession Police's closure of the United Chinese National Products Mall was copied and sent for review and reply.' It is learned that this case has been repeatedly petitioned by the mall to request negotiations and prevent the matter from reaching the government. The Public Concession Council unilaterally ordered the closure due to the licensing issue of the mall's attached entertainment section and closed it. The prior failure to request the court's permission and rash execution was a fundamental error, which not only hinders our national legal rights, but also violates the agreement of the Shanghai Public Concession Special District Court. The Secretariat of this government has been ordered to send a letter to protest the Public Concession Council. You are hereby informed and hope you will take note."

Citizens' Assembly The first branch of the Citizens' Federation convened a citizens' assembly at 2:00 PM yesterday, attended by over 100 representatives from the Citizens' General Association, Samsung Factory, Sanyou Company, Guanshengyuan, Lao Jiuzhang, etc. Zhou Jucun was elected chairman and Ni Jilian recorded. First, the chairman reported the reason for the meeting, followed by Zhang Zilian's report on the circumstances of being ordered to close by the Public Works Department. Zhang Yichen of the Municipal General Association then gave guidance, and the discussion and proposals immediately followed. The proposal that the Citizens' Assembly member National Products Mall was illegally closed by the Public Works Department, how should it be corrected, prevent the Public Works Department from having any further illegal incidents in the future, and resolve the citizens' pain was resolved as follows: (1) Send a letter to the General Assembly to unite various organizations and convene a city-wide citizens' assembly; (2) Representatives will be elected by the city-wide citizens' assembly to petition in Beijing; (3) Negotiate by telecommunications; (4) Suggest that the General Assembly discuss the recovery of the concession using effective methods at the meeting.

Wang Yansong Talks About the Native Bank Law

Still Hopeful That the Government Can Adopt It

Regarding the issue of the Native Bank Law, the city's Native Bank Association still needs to convene a committee meeting to discuss the reasons for continuing the petition and request the government to enact it. The reporter from New Sound Newspaper had previously submitted a proposal to the National Assembly by the Native Bank Association. After Mr. Wang Yansong, who attended as a representative, explained the reasons to various parties in Beijing, the result was satisfactory. Therefore, Mr. Wang must be very concerned about this matter. Therefore, he visited Mr. Wang yesterday and asked for his opinion. According to his reply, when he attended the National Assembly, the Native Bank did have this proposal. At that time, he believed that if this case was observed from Shanghai, it would be a problem for a part of Shanghai, but native banks were everywhere in the provinces, cities, counties, and towns across the country, and were related to commerce and agriculture. Therefore, observed from another perspective, it was a national economic issue, so it was possible to submit it to the National Assembly. However, after he arrived in Beijing, he felt that the National Assembly's discussion was focused on the provisional constitution, and there were many other proposals for unification and construction. In addition, the meeting period was urgent, and he was afraid that if the Native Bank Law was proposed, there might not be time to discuss it. Therefore, he separately explained to the Central Party Headquarters, Legislative Yuan President Shao, and various committee members that it was necessary to separately legislate the Native Bank Law and asked for its adoption. At that time, the Central Party Headquarters and President Shao believed that it had research value and agreed to consider it. He believed that since this matter had hope of achieving its goal, there was no need to submit it to the National Assembly again. Afterwards, he returned to Shanghai and saw in the newspaper that the Native Bank Law had been passed by the Legislative Yuan meeting and handed over to the Commercial Law Committee for drafting. He was hoping that it would be enacted and implemented as soon as possible. Unexpectedly, he later saw Mr. Ma Yinchu's opinion, believing that there was no need to separately legislate the Native Bank Law. The starting point of his advocacy was still the position of the bank. In fact, banks in China today are still in their infancy and cannot meet the needs of economic circulation in agriculture and commerce. Moreover, the nature of native banks is different from that of banks. Mr. Qin Runqing, the leader of the native bank industry, explained it in detail. Therefore, he very much hopes that the government will adopt it when the industry continues to request it, that is, legislate it separately, so as not to force the native bank industry to use the Banking Law and suffer the pain of cutting its feet to fit the shoes. To the best of his ability, he is still willing to support it in order to achieve its goal, he said.

Death of Chu Minyi's Father

Central Committee member Chu Minyi was previously dispatched by the Central Government to Xinjiang to inspect Party affairs. Simultaneously, he was also recommended by the Chinese Academic Association as the leader of the Chinese contingent of the Sino-French Academic Investigation Group. He departed last month and is currently on a long journey. Unexpectedly, his respected father, Mr. Xing Tian, passed away at his native Nanzun at 5 AM on the 19th (the day before yesterday), at the age of 77. Mr. Chu is not in Shanghai, so his wife has rushed to handle the funeral arrangements. A telegram has also been sent to the French Embassy in Beijing, forwarding it to the Sino-French Academic Investigation Group, urging Mr. Chu to return home as soon as possible.

Request for Tax Exemption on Sand Cloth and Native Cloth

Document Submitted to the Central Government

The Sand Cloth and Native Cloth Trade Association of this city yesterday submitted separate requests to the National Government, the Ministry of Finance, and the Consolidated Tax Bureau, requesting a clear order to the entire country to refer to established cases and grant tax exemptions. The original submission stated: "Regarding the matter of native cloth tax exemption, we request that the Ministry of Finance issue an order to the National Consolidated Tax Bureau and the Customs Administration to refer to the resolution of the National Government in the 16th year of the Republic of China and issue a clear order to the entire country to grant tax exemptions, in order to maintain commerce and broaden the people's livelihood. It is noted that our fellow native cloth traders in Shanghai transport and sell handwoven native cloth for export. The National Government has long issued a clear order for tax exemption nationwide. This year, the Jiangsu-Zhejiang-Anhui Consolidated Tax Bureau was established, adopting a one-item-one-tax system. An order was issued to levy taxes based on tax regulations. A request was made on behalf of the poor and impoverished people of the country to exempt them from tariffs. On May 19th of the 20th year, the Ministry of Finance approved the exemption, and the Customs Administration issued an order to all customs houses to exempt export taxes. It has been found that most of the native cloth produced in Jiangsu, transshipped through Shanghai, and exported to other provinces is for the needs of the people of eastern provinces. Yingkou is a transshipment area. The people of the north are more frugal than those in the south and have a high degree of patriotism. They regard this Jiangsu-produced native cloth as an extremely important item, valued for its durable material. In the past 20 years, although imported cloth from overseas is far inferior in material durability to domestic goods, its price is lower than that of domestic goods. Native cloth has suffered a severe blow from this, facing a state of decline. Fortunately, the National Government issued an order for tax exemption, and the people promoted domestic goods. Cooperation between officials and the people served as an invisible force to resist foreign goods, in an attempt to remedy the situation. It can be seen that tax reduction and exemption, and the promotion of domestic goods, are essential factors in awakening the people's hearts, especially concerning the southern industry. If overseas cloth expands its sales channels, directly absorbing the money of the eastern provinces, it will endanger the livelihood of the poor people of Jiangsu Province, harming both sides. It is almost too late. Recently, a letter from Zhu Limen, a merchant in Yingkou, stated that the merchants and people of the northern provinces, knowing that tariffs have been exempted, cannot bear any further burdens on this native cloth. Goods transported from the southern provinces have been stopped from being unloaded, affecting silver reserves and the market, with some even advocating suspending transportation at the expense of business. They have called for assistance from fellow traders in Shanghai. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce has sent a telegram to the government of the eastern provinces and the Department of Finance, requesting that the authorities consider the poor people of both supply and demand sides, who are happy to promote domestic goods, and appreciate their patriotic enthusiasm. Based on the principle that taxes are collected from factories and based on the yarn, this native cloth is a type of cotton fabric, within the scope of the consolidated tax regulations for cotton yarn. According to the national tax interpretation of one item, one tax, it is a cotton product directly woven from cotton yarn that has already been subjected to consolidated tax. It should be allowed to be sold without further taxation, except for business tax, which is a local tax revenue. It seems impossible to levy it again. We dare to express our opinions in detail, hoping that the government will uphold the National Government's goal of saving the country and the people, and consider the unemployment of the poor. An uneasy silence, we dare to lay it out. Humbly beseeching consideration and approval, recognizing that the rights and interests lost after tax exemption are not a small matter, allowing for the issuance of a clear order to the national tax collection agencies to maintain the established case, which will truly benefit both the national economy and the people's livelihood."

The Japanese Ministry of Commerce and Industry is strongly encouraging Japanese merchants to establish factories in China. Condition of Japanese Spring Cocoons This Year

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau's Raw Silk Inspection Office yesterday received a report from Japan regarding the condition of spring cocoons this year, stating: "According to the results of the previous survey released by the Japanese Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry, the estimated production of spring cocoons in the 24 prefectures of the early group at the end of May is 1,383,265 dan, a decrease of 200,951 dan compared to the actual amount collected last year (a decrease of approximately 12%). However, in the Kanto region, where new cocoons have already entered the market, and in the Hokuriku region, which will gradually enter the market in the future, the government has ordered restrictions on the amount of silkworm eggs collected. At the same time, insufficient fertilizer application in the gardens and reduced leaf production will result in a decrease of more than 15% in the national spring cocoon harvest compared to last year."

Book Industry Resolves to Increase Prices

Effective July 1st

The case of the binding industry in this city requesting an increase in prices has been in dispute for a long time and has not yet been resolved. It is now heard that this case has been discussed in detail by the executive committee of the Book Industry Association. The previous labor unrest in the binding industry was caused by some binders underbidding for business and others paying low wages and recruiting many apprentices, leading to worker dissatisfaction and disputes. The association's investigation found that without a unified approach, those with little capital would bid lower, while those with more capital would bid higher, affecting both the livelihood of workers and hindering the printing and publishing business. For the sake of fairness and long-term stability, the following measures have been decided: A. Western binding: A single leaf of single-sided printing in Western binding is equivalent to half a page of traditional binding. In the past, there were few binding machines and few people who could make books, so the price was higher than traditional binding. The common price for binding works sold to the book industry was 7.5 to 8 jiao per 10,000 leaves, but some reduced it to 6.5 jiao, and some were as high as 9 jiao. Now, it is proposed to increase the price.

Free Talk

World Anecdotes

— Haike

The authorities in Mannheim, Germany, seeing the prevalence of idlers in the city, came up with a funny way to crack down on them. They sent policemen with a large cart of chairs to patrol the streets. Whenever they saw idlers standing around on the street corners, they would take a chair from the cart and invite them to sit down. This caused onlookers to laugh, and the idlers would retreat in shame.

A large British railway company employs inspection specialists to thoroughly inspect everything used by the company. Their work is often comical, such as counting the number of bristles in a broom or picking out the cotton threads mixed in with a wool carpet. This kind of work is very tedious, but it is their job.

The number of married couples in the United States who do not have children is about four times higher in cities than in rural areas. It is said that this is an example of urban hygiene being inferior to that of the countryside.

A rubber company in Liverpool, England, employs two women. Whenever a new type of rubber shoe is made, the two of them wear them and walk back and forth to show customers. It is estimated that the two women walked about 12,000 miles in four years.

A Trip to Guangzhou

— Ji

I have been in Guangzhou for more than twenty days. Although the prosperous commerce is inferior to that of Shanghai and Hong Kong, it does not receive the slightest assistance from foreigners. It is entirely self-operated by Chinese people. Guangzhou can be truly proud of this.

"Eat in Guangzhou." Therefore, there are especially many restaurants and teahouses in Guangzhou. But Guangzhou people call eating a meal "drinking tea." Teahouses also sell meals. There are two kinds of eating. "Small eat" is only drinking tea and eating in the teahouse, costing at most four jiao, which is already enough. "Big eat" is a full table of dishes, which costs at least twenty or thirty yuan.

Everything is done in Hao dollars. There are only Guangdong double-jiao coins. The front side has a small portrait of Mr. Sun Yat-sen. The reverse side is double ears of rice. One dollar is five jiao. If Hong Kong dollars and silver dollars are used, then they must be converted according to market prices. In the current market, one Hong Kong dollar is worth about thirteen hao. One silver dollar is worth about eleven hao. If you go to Hong Kong, then only Hong Kong dollars and Hong Kong dimes are used in the market. Those who only have silver dollars must first exchange them for Hong Kong dollars before they can use them. Therefore, there are especially many exchange shops in Hong Kong.

The most popular thing in Guangzhou is "midnight snack." This "midnight snack" is not the midnight snack that Shanghai people order in Guangdong restaurants in winter, which consists of a charcoal brazier and a few plates of raw fish. It is a casual name for a small snack. Some people even eat a twenty or thirty yuan banquet at eleven or twelve o'clock at night, also called a midnight snack. "Eat in Guangzhou" shows how important Guangzhou people consider "eating."

Guangzhou people not only value eating, but also value entertainment. After dinner at six o'clock and before the midnight snack comes on the market at eleven o'clock, they must watch a big opera (Cantonese opera) and Yinghua (movies). In Guangzhou, the most famous big theater is the "Haizhu Theater" on Changdi. Famous opera troupes consider it an honor to perform at the "Haizhu" if they come to Guangzhou. Jue Xiansheng of the Cantonese troupe (Xue Juexian, i.e., Zhang Fei in Shanghai), whose supporting actors include the Hua Dan Sao Yunlan and the Sheng actors Chen Jintang and Lin Kunshan (first-class Haizhu seats cost three yuan). Riyuexing, Renshou Nian, Mei Lanfang of the Beijing troupe, and the Meihua Dance Troupe have all performed here. The next best are the "Taiping Theater" (Zhang Huichong's magic has performed here) and the "Henan Theater." There are countless movie theaters. Recently, they are competing to install sound equipment. The ones that already have sound are "Zhonghua," "Xin Guomin," "Mofan," "Mingzhu," "Yonghan," and "Nanguan." The sound films shown are best at "Zhonghua," "Yonghan," and "Mingzhu." There are as many as eight silent movie theaters. Most of the films shown are domestic. Therefore, the business of sound movie theaters is even more genuine.

There are more than twenty newspapers in Guangzhou. The source of news, in addition to exclusive telegrams and investigations, often publishes materials from Shanghai and Hong Kong newspapers. The three with larger sales are "Guohua," "Minguo," and "Gongping." "Guohua" is well-organized. "Gongping" has an old mind. Sales are all around 10,000 copies. There are very few good materials in the supplements. Some supplements published an article transcribed from a Hong Kong

newspaper. Who knew that this article in the Hong Kong newspaper was transcribed from this talk. There are many, many jokes like this. The most prosperous market is on "Changdi." The next best are "Yonghan Road," "Xinxin Road," and "Xidi." Large hotels like "Dongya," "Zhongshan," "Xinya," and "Asia" are all on the two banks of Changxi. The night view is also the best on these two banks.

The only school for studying drama is "Guangdong Drama Institute," which is sponsored by the provincial government. The appointed director is Mr. Ouyang Yuqian. The teachers inside, such as Mr. Tang Huaiqiu, Yan Gongshang, and Hu Chunbing, are all very knowledgeable in drama. On June 1st, their first drama troupe was established. They performed at the Provincial Education Association for ten days. The programs performed included "Camellia," "Selling and Buying," "Married People," and "The Bear." I went to see it several times with my colleague Shi Shuming. Among the performing students, the best were Ms. Gao Weilan and Ms. Peng Guohua. The next best were Mr. Zhang Zhengfan, Mr. Li Chenfeng, Mr. Zhao Rulin, and Mr. Chen You. Ms. Qu Ai was also good. Mr. Lu Dun, because he could not get rid of the "martial" air during the performance, was ultimately inferior to Mr. Zhang and Mr. Li. Otherwise, he would also be a performing talent.

A Record of Wang Shizi's Painting Exhibition

— Zhu Jue

Wang Shizi of Jurong exhibited his latest works at the Ningbo Fellow Association. There are one hundred and fifty frames. Flowers, birds, insects, and fish are all beautiful. Generally speaking, what is most unmatched in Shizi's paintings are three points. For example, the wetness of the brush is able to restrain, the color is beautiful and unconventional, and the ink is light and spiritual. It is enough to show that the energy is full and the operation is miserable. The mood of the exhibition, such as the rose chicken, bean worm, double carp, willow emerald bird, and the lone egret in the sunset, is clear and far away. The creation of the carving column white dove and the willow swing is novel. The ink bird tree is vast and noble. Standing for thousands of years. In addition, the collections of Zhongding and Han Dynasty are linked together. The brushstrokes are vertical and horizontal. The ancient interest is full of fun. The painting is small. The elegance of the situation is also the choice of the time. The ancients called the talent of the eight buckets many. I also sigh that the art of Shizi is many.

A Brief Discussion on the Japanese Film Industry

— Li Taoan

The center of the Japanese film industry is in Tokyo, especially in the Asakusa area of Asakusa Park. Almost all of them are movie theaters. The films that are shown there, except for their own country, are only those Western sound and silent films. There is still its power. Speaking of our Chinese films, it is simply not visible. This is not because Chinese films are not good or what. Really. They have a strong sense of patriotism and cannot bear to let their rights and interests flow out, so they will show films from other countries to destroy their original great cause. As for Western films, they can still maintain their lives, but it is related to the relationship between their overseas Chinese and the international status, forming a relative proportion.

However. The films they produce themselves implicitly suggest two different factions. One is dedicated to propaganda for the capitalist class. The other is the vanguard of the laboring class. As long as you look at the film, you can see the strong colors of each faction. Therefore, it can be said that their films do contain a huge role in terms of ideology.

Although Japan is a constitutional monarchy, the power of the common people is also very common. The price of seats in their movie theaters is probably only 50 Japanese sen. (Approximately equal to one yuan of national currency.) Upstairs and downstairs are completely the same. Arbitrary seating. Regardless of rank. Although this is one of their characteristics. However, due to the architectural relationship. So as long as you pay such a considerable price. No matter upstairs or downstairs. What you get is always the same joy.

Some people say. The development of the Japanese film industry is also inevitable. One is because their people's patriotism. And the heart of cherishing their own emerging industries is too heavy. The result should be like this. The second is due to the increase in the number of theaters opened throughout the country. In its own country. There is excess sales. Some are not affected by business. Also. The government and the public opinion side. They are all giving considerable help. And sympathetic encouragement. So that they can safely soar upwards. Striving to make progress forward. Is also a major reason.

Research on Famine Food (Part 2)

— Tian Xu I Sheng

The fourth prescription says: Wash and steam sweet potatoes until half-dry. Mash them. Add glutinous rice porridge and mix like mud. Coat them on bamboo fences. The longer they are there, the stronger they become. They will not be infested with insects or damaged. If there is a famine, take a piece the size of a hand and cook it into a large pot of thin porridge. Eating it can withstand hunger. Or make them into brick shapes and build them into walls for future use. According to my research, sweet potatoes are probably red-hearted sweet potatoes. However, the scientific name is 非薯, while those called 薯 are 薯芋, which is taro. The Records of the Grand Historian by Zhuo Wenjun says, "Below Mount Min, there are野有蹲鴟, and one will not be hungry until death."野有蹲鴟 is taro. It is a description of its shape. However, the nutrients contained in taro are actually more than in 非薯. A comparison is listed on the left:

Item Name: 蛋白質 (Protein) 脂肪 (Fat) 澱粉 (Starch) 水分 (Water) Remarks

8.1 7.4 3.678 397.68 Fresh ones, four catties can抵 (compare) to one catty of rice, one catty of dried flour can compare to two catties of rice.

芋 (Taro) 165.072 107.82 456.x Fresh ones, one catty four ounces can compare to one catty of rice, one catty of dried flour can compare to four and a half catties of rice.

As the above comparison shows, the effect of taro flour is actually stronger than that of 非薯 flour. The sweet potatoes used in the fourth prescription refer to taro. There are originally two types of taro, red and white. The white ones have thin skins and are white. They are used as vegetables. The red ones have thick, hairy skins with a light purple color. These are hairy taro. Both of these are sold by stalls in Hangzhou to provide food for laborers. The former is called baked sweet potatoes, and the latter is called taro. Their prices are very low. Looking at the above, it is known that the famine relief methods recorded in "Yan Fang Xin Bian" are not absurd and can be used in practice. During the famine relief period, those who are interested can pay attention to this. However, it is easy for the hungry to choke if they eat too much. It is up to the authorities to give good advice and impose restrictions to avoid abuses. "Yan Fang Xin Bian" also explains this in detail.

Rotary Club of Speech Fiction

Three Eras (12)

— Zhang Henshui

(6) Commander Zhang Revisits the Old Place

After Zhang Xiaosan left Beijing, he traveled east, west, north, and south, fighting many battles. Each time he fought, Zhang Xiaosan was promoted one step at a time. He was promoted to company commander. Suddenly, after a rebellion, he was promoted to regimental commander. After becoming a regimental commander, after a rebellion, he was promoted to division commander. After becoming a division commander, he became much freer. At this time, their inspector was stationed in Beijing. Zhang Xiaosan came to Beijing to ask for instructions. He actually came back as an official. After returning, he borrowed a house from a friend to live in. He borrowed a big house on Nongshangbu Street. When he took the car to see the new house, it was extremely coincidental. It was the big red door where he used to sing sour plum soup. For many years, he had been watching the people living in it. That kind of rich energy was really annoying. But now it seems that it cannot be considered annoying. If you have money, you should not live in a good house, but in a broken house. On the same day, Zhang Xiaosan looked at the house and thought it was satisfactory. He moved in. Then, the two concubines he had acquired in other provinces also came. The police district nearby, in order to protect the national defender, temporarily added a police post at the gate of Commander Zhang's mansion. Whether Zhang Xiaosan went out early in the morning or came back late at night, even in strong winds and heavy rains, he always saw a policeman standing outside the door. Moreover, he would respectfully salute. He thought, "People have earned me a lot of money." He really felt a little uneasy. Therefore, he wanted to reward him with some money. But he did not say it. At this time, Zhang Xiaosan did not hate the police. He felt that he relied on the police for help in many places. It was just that his wife thought that he would not become an official. At this time, he had to find her and let her see. For this reason, he took the car to the original compound to take a look. The residents, seeing a military officer with four box-carrying guards walking in, shrank into their houses and did not dare to come out. Zhang Xiaosan stood in the courtyard and explained the origin in detail. Then, an old shoe cobbler first peered through the window and saw clearly. Then, he came out, standing more than ten feet away from Zhang Xiaosan, squatted down and smiled and squatted at him. He laughed. "I didn't expect it. Zhang is a commander. The neighbors have all moved away. Only my family is old. Zhang Commander. You still remember the old neighbors. Really good. My Zhang Lord." Zhang Xiaosan said, "Do you know where my wife went from before? I... I want to see her." The shoe cobbler said, "Zhang Commander. What are you planning to do?" Zhang Xiaosan said, "I wow. Hmph." The shoe maker said, "We haven't seen him for two years. Do you think he can still come here? Sir. Have a bowl of water." Zhang Xiaosan was polite and sent the old shoe cobbler twenty yuan. He left.

Youth Garden

About the Public Performance of "Stormy Wind and Rain"

Letter from Mr. Gu Jianchen

To Brother Yingpeng,

This is our second report on the performance of our plays. The first was "A Patriotic Heart" by Xiong Fuxi, which achieved great success in Zhenjiang and Wuxi. Now, this second report concerns the performance of "Stormy Wind and Rain."

The 13th and 14th of this month were the dates for the third achievement exhibition of our Jiangsu Provincial College of Education, divided into static exhibitions and dynamic performances. Naturally, the public performance of a play belongs to the dynamic achievements. As I direct the drama here, this responsibility naturally falls on me. When we started preparing the script, everyone wanted to see a famous play and perform "Lady Windermere's Fan." However, difficulties arose due to casting and costume issues, and selecting a play almost became a problem. I can barely write a few scripts myself, but because my learning is insufficient, I always find them superficial and childish. I originally didn't plan to use my own play as a script. However, many good friends encouraged me this time, complimenting me as the Tian Han of the College of Education, saying that Tian Han can write and perform his own plays. So, I had to shamelessly try to imitate Tian Han. Fortunately, after the performance of "The Unfinished Tombstone," people have a considerable understanding of theatrical techniques, so I dared to boldly put "Stormy Wind and Rain" into rehearsal. This script depicts a national movement arising from the interactions of China, Korea, and Japan. It has three acts in total. A brief explanation is as follows:

(Act One) In the evening, in the garden of the old bureaucrat Zhao Jingxiong's house in Qingdao, it depicts the beauty trap used by the Japanese to deliberately undermine the patriotic work of the Chinese people, and the failure of their attempt to bribe Zhao Jingxiong, as well as the successful theft of maps and plans for exploiting Manchuria and Mongolia.

(Act Two) The morning two days later, at the Liang family's residence, it depicts the successful Japanese plan to frame Yang Zhiqing. His fiancée, Miss Yongfen, forced by patriotic indignation, cancels their engagement.

(Act Three) This act takes place in a hospital ward.

Yang Zhiqing, due only to a minor oversight, is vilified as a traitor. As a result, he develops a heart ailment and is sent here for treatment. We see how the Japanese woman, Ono Umeko, suddenly transforms into a Korean and repents before being killed, how Miss Liang Yongfen reunites with Yang Zhiqing, and how he goes mad and commits suicide. All of this is made clear in this act.

The casting for this play is very appropriate. Introductions are as follows:

Yang Zhiqing…Chen Guoli

Ono Umeko…Ye Yunzhen

Zhao Gui…Huang Xie

Liu Guojun…Jin Fenggang

Zhao Yangxiuzhen…Chen Zuying

Zhao Jingxiong…Li Bingming

Xin Erlang…Tong Jingsan

Liang Zhong…Song Chengde

Liang Yongfen…Mao Jingzhen

Lin Cheng…Gu Chi

Liang Jingde…Hua Wuquei

Doctor Zhang…Xie Boming

Female Nurse…Zhang Zhenhua

The entire cast includes Tong Jingsan, Chen Zuying, and Chen Guoli, who are famous for their performances in "Blood Flowers," and Ye Yunzhen, who is famous for his performance in "A Patriotic Heart." All of them play important roles this time. Mao Jingzhen is also an outstanding talent among the female students, but she has never been on stage here before. This is her first time, and she is playing the main character. Her diligence, obedience, and talent have brought her great success.

The scenery and lighting have also been greatly improved. We made a new set and a garden backdrop. The other sets are modified from "Blood Flowers." Designed and supervised by drawing teacher Mr. Wu Shuyang, they are rich and beautiful. We know that lighting is the soul of drama, so we abolished the rigid footlights and overhead lights and used [whitespace] to control them. In this respect, the beauty of the play has indeed been greatly enhanced. For example, the sunset in Act One, with amber light projected from the left stage corner, makes the colors of the scenery particularly harmonious. The second scene of Act One is an evening scene, using blue light, and we also made a fake moon. This arrangement is said to be the first of its kind on the Wuxi stage. (Someone came and asked me what the moon was made of. I honestly replied that it was made from the small hat box of political science professor Mr. Chen Shoutong.) The only pity is that we didn't have [whitespace], so the sunset in Act One could not be fully realized. (The Shanghai Drama Association originally had two, and I went to Shanghai to borrow them from Mr. Ying Yunwei, but he said they were not repaired. Later, I wrote two letters to ask him, saying that it would be great to borrow them if possible, and if not, please write back. But he greatly disappointed me by not telling me a single word. He probably understands a bit of economics now and is reluctant to spend even four cents on postage.) In the future, we plan to make two ourselves, to avoid so much trouble borrowing from others.

After this public performance, many colleagues came to congratulate me on my success. I felt even more ashamed. As for the hard work of the staff, I should also report that to you. During the public performance, I stood entirely in the position of director, letting the students handle the stage work themselves. The stage management and lighting by Mr. Zeng Lu, the prop management by Mr. Gu Chi and Mr. Chen Tingsheng, and the scenery by Mr. Miao Jingyi, Mr. Zhou Shunyuan, Mr. Song Chengde, and Mr. Gu Defu were all much improved compared to the "Blood Flowers" era. In terms of makeup, several people were able to do it themselves. Miss Qin Xiangsun also learned makeup and helped me dress them up.

I sent you the script for "Stormy Wind and Rain" earlier. I hope you will combine "The Unfinished Tombstone," "Father's Daughter," and "Child of the Motherland" into a single volume. We will discuss other matters later. I wish you health.

Gu Jianchen, June 16th

A Few Words After Watching "Mei Luoxiang"

— Ke

The Central Public Drama Society's "Mei Luoxiang," which had been brewing for a long time, finally met us last Wednesday afternoon. This is truly a gratifying event. In particular, we respect Mr. Ouyang Xin's perseverance. His father had only died a few days before, and he was able to suppress his grief, so that this budding flower of art would not wither because of him.

The curtain opened, and scene after scene passed before our eyes. The plot is roughly as follows:

Mei Luoxiang is a beautiful, young, and weak-willed actress. She has been living a life of luxury, dependent on a wealthy businessman, Bai Senqing. Later, she falls in love with a newspaper reporter, Ma Ziying. However, Ma Ziying is very poor and cannot achieve their desired goal for the time being. This forces him to leave her to develop his intended career.

After she and Ma Ziying become engaged, she behaves herself. On the one hand, she rejects Bai Senqing's material assistance, and on the other hand, she works hard to make a living on her own. This forces her to get closer to hardship day by day, and eventually, she cannot survive even after pawning all her clothes. Her friend, Xiao Chunlan, uses this opportunity to persuade her to return to Bai Senqing. She is moved by the sweet words. Then, Bai Senqing forces her to write a letter breaking off with Ziying. However, she did not do so. She burned the letter.

Soon, Ma Ziying returns, wealthy, to take her. Bai Senqing announces their past relationship and says that she has deceived two men at the same time. As a result, Ma Ziying and Bai Senqing both abandon her, causing her to eventually fall into depravity.

The best performance in the entire play goes to Ms. Wang Hualian, who plays Granny Gui. She can forget herself and merge with the character in the play. When she is reluctant to leave her mistress, Mei Luoxiang, she tells of her hardships. She cries, crying with tears and snot, and the muscles on her shoulders and back twitch involuntarily. Even more interesting is her Hefei dialect.

The second best performance goes to Mr. Ouyang Xin's Bai Senqing. He vividly brings a generous businessman to the stage. His dialogue is clear and loud, and his gestures are neither artificial nor unnatural. Although his facial expressions are not very attentive, he can be said to be a success.

Mr. Zhang Liangyi's Ma Ziying's dialogue is as stiff as a primary school student reciting a textbook. What is even more unsatisfactory is that face, smeared with the makeup of a young man from an old opera stage, and those two hands always stuck in his pockets. His facial expressions never changed at all. These things make the audience feel that he is just himself and has nothing to do with the play.

The lead role, Mei Luoxiang, is played by Ms. Zhang Zhaohe. Her shortcoming is that, from the opening to the closing, her hands are always crossed. When Ma Ziying returns successful, the plot should be tense. But our Miss Zhang always remains indifferent and does not show the slightest surprise.

In addition, Fan Zhen's Qin Jingtian is not an important role, and his performance is passable. Xiao Chunlan is more important. She is played by Ms. Zhu Qin, who is dignified, so her attitude is incompatible with the romantic Xiao Chunlan. In the dialogue persuading Mei Luoxiang, there is no action expression, and the voice is so low that it is indistinguishable.

Originally, art is not an easy thing to succeed in. The selection of the script must take into account the cast. If we can't find someone to play a romantic woman, we can choose another script. We must never be vague and compromise, leading to the failure of the entire play.

Going back to the topic, in this era of decline in Chinese art—especially drama—of course, we cannot expect to achieve satisfactory results with the first experience. What we need is the enthusiastic promotion of those who love art, so that the general public understands that drama is the education of the people, and concentrates their energy to irrigate the root of this art, so that it can blossom into brilliant flowers. Therefore, although this public performance is a failure in terms of artistic achievement, it has a very determined spirit in the entire drama movement. Like the director, Mr. Gu Zhongyi, for a month or two, he ran from Zhenru to Baotaiwan regardless of wind or rain. And all the actors sacrificed their precious time to rehearse when the big exam was approaching. This point alone is very touching to us for their artistic spirit.

Farewell

— Wen

The domineering hot summer will soon be upon us. Therefore, the impression of the two words "graduation" is more deeply imprinted on the hearts of that part of the so-called "silver-plated graduates." When stepping out of the hall where the solemn graduation ceremony is held, the heart cannot help but throb, as if suffering an attack of melancholy. Inside the hall, it is harmonious and lively, listening with relish to the instructions of teachers and elders. But after the ceremony, walking out of the gate, it seems that I have suddenly lost something, and I can't help but lower my head and become disheartened. Two eyes full of hot tears are about to burst forth, as if I have been sentenced by criminal law.

What is the reason for this common state? Yes, simply put, it is the "way out" problem that is the price of four years of university life. When not yet graduated, one always feels that society is so vast. Can't it accommodate one person? That's right, expectations for the future are extremely optimistic, and even for those "predecessors" who generally look for a job to make a living, they express all sorts of sarcastic words, such as "rice buckets, such incompetent failures." But when it is my turn to participate in the graduation ceremony, these unsympathetic words will be put on my own head. What else can I say? Don't blame the heavens, don't blame others. But the "way out" has indeed become a problem. How heroic is that silhouette wearing a square cap, but what's the use of that? Aren't you seeing disappointment? If, unfortunately, after a month or two... there is no way to ask people for help in the east, and there is no response to asking people for help in the west. Needless to say, one is anxious. Asking about the result of "silver-plating" is this ending. How can the annoyance be described? Under such a multi-faceted concern, the so-called graduation may not become a happy and exciting event.

I have asked several classmates who are about to graduate about what they will do after graduation. They either say that it is undecided or that there is no way. And their words are full of disappointment. Such a disappointing downturn is really so boring. But we can only be bored. In fact, I know the seriousness of this "way out" problem. Today it has become universal. The current social environment is worth discussing at length. We don't need to talk about any theories. The facts are very clearly laid out in front of us. A large batch of square-capped "silver-plated" bachelors pours out from the sacred halls of learning. It is said that they are "seeking welfare for society," but in fact, where does society need them? I simply don't have enough words to describe it.

But then again, thinking realistically, modern education is becoming increasingly capitalized. The burden of studying has been squeezed to the point of exhaustion. One hopes to receive some profits after graduation, but who knows that one cannot even recover the capital today. Then, is this ultimately the uselessness of the university students themselves, or the uselessness of the nature of the university? These things are long to say and inevitably have a bias. Let's all understand this in our own hearts. However, if we want to curse, then let's first despise ourselves by three points, to show that we are not guilty, and then let's vent some anger, because having the urge to seek knowledge is the first wrong.

Why don't I reflect on myself, what is the so-called four-year university education? From running into the university with ulterior motives to wearing the square cap, what exactly has been given during this period? In other words, what has been gained? In my estimation, perhaps very few people can answer. I remember a magazine essay contest, "What has university education given you?" The result was that nothing was gained. Everything was as empty as if they had not entered university. We should applaud such a true confession. Someone once satirized, "To ask how well the university students have done in four years, one can use the amount of money they have spent as corroborating evidence and a ratio." That is, two hundred in the first year, four hundred in the second year, eight hundred in the third year, and one thousand six hundred in the fourth year. Well then, let me ask... I think that's probably insulting.

I seem to often have a contradictory opposite question. On the one hand, I feel that "silver-plated" university education is not enough, as if it must be "gold-plated." On the other hand, I feel that such mass production of "silver-plating" is already intimidating in terms of social use. There's no way to talk about "gold-plating." Such a conflict is really impossible to resolve. This is because the characteristics of the current Chinese education system are too intriguing, too amusing.

However, this question is of course only the panicked mentality of an ungraduated person. As I see the summer approaching day by day, I can't help but be moved in my heart. Many friends will end their university student days to find a way out. The portraits of them in square caps are all taken very neatly, but these are only superficial pleasures. Their inner distress is increasing day by day. A shadow tightly covers their hearts. It seems that they are very reluctant to end this life. At the same time, this "silver-plated" life will only be a short year for me. The journey has reached the last stage, especially giving me a feeling of unbearable sympathy. It's a pity that I am a person who cannot paint, otherwise, I would definitely paint a few allegorical paintings to express my vigorous emotions. Therefore, I can only borrow some of the above words to offer and express a fraction of my feelings. But the above words are definitely not able to fully express this issue. For the sake of length, I will leave it to another opportunity to supplement. My original intention is still to say farewell, to the "silver-plated" bachelors who will graduate in the summer.

Finally, I would like to add these two words as a farewell and memorial, "Treasure it."

Shanghai Market

Commercial News

The New New Company on Nanjing Road announced that the company's main newspaper, the New New Daily, is the only literary daily in Shanghai. Edited by Mr. Feng Shuren and Mr. Xia Tianwu, it is making every effort to promote new literature. The contents of this newspaper are elegant and beautiful, and have long been praised by readers. It also has many supplements, such as the Crazy Current poetry special, the Bodhi Weekly, and Qing Sheng, etc. The writing of each has its own strengths, adding to the brilliance. Recently, in order to promote literature and art, it is widely recruiting subscribers. If you request a sample newspaper, please attach four cents in postage, and a volume will be sent immediately.

The Wing On Company on Nanjing Road announced that many new seasonal goods have recently been put on the market, such as various seasonal foods in the southern goods department, various gift candies in the candy department, etc. In addition, the various hams of the southern goods are also at a special price of 15% off, to facilitate the use of gift-giving by the general public. At the same time, a large number of vacuum hot and cold bottles have newly arrived in the water bottle department. The construction of this type of hot and cold bottle is extremely perfect. Used to store cold and hot items, it can maintain the original temperature for more than 24 hours, etc.

Theater News

The Hua Drama Company announced that the success of the company's "King of Ten Thousand Envoys" has truly exhausted the director Zhang Huimin's efforts and shattered the protagonist Wu Xixin's heart and soul. The purity of the content and the depth of expression dare to say that it is the king of domestic martial arts films. Anyone who has already appreciated the performances of Mr. Zhang and Mr. Wu will naturally make further admiration. Therefore, on the first day of the public screening, people marveled and said it was amazing, and every performance was sold out. From this, it can be seen that the reputation is not false.
